In addition, the city encourages the development of retention facilities in such a manner that they will become aesthetically and recreationally beneficial to the community in which they are located; and 
(8)	To require any development to retain any runoff which exceeds an allowable increase of one cubic foot per second per acre caused by the development and to utilize the parking area or privately owned retention/detention facility. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 6) 
Secs. 16-377—16-395. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PLAN SUBMISSION AND REVIEW 

Sec. 16-396. - Standards. 
All persons proposing development or construction shall, prior to beginning any construction activity, submit to the county engineering department site plans prepared in accordance with this article illustrating the means by which conformance with this article is to be achieved and illustrating compliance with applicable development standards before issuance of a development or building permit. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 20) 
Sec. 16-397. - Utilities. 
Electric, telephone and gas utilities shall submit plans and obtain a development permit only for major transmission installations located within rights-of-way or easements devoted exclusively to installations of utility facilities. Individual single-family lots within approved subdivisions shall be exempt from these requirements for new residential construction, with the exception of individual single-family lots located within the 100-year floodplain which shall be subject to review and approval in accordance with this and other applicable code provisions. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 20) 
Sec. 16-398. - Grading and drainage. 
The grading and drainage portion of a site plan shall be prepared under the supervision of a currently licensed state-registered professional engineer. The plan shall include a site location map of the project area indicating the location of the project in relation to rivers and streams, a topographic map showing existing and proposed contours at one-foot intervals, proposed drainageways and drainage structures, in addition to the requirements established in other ordinances. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 20) 
Sec. 16-399. - Hydraulics/hydrologic engineering. 
When the hydraulic/hydrologic engineering analysis includes applications of the principles of flood routing, super critical flow, high-energy dissipation or conversion, backwater curves, floodplain studies or other advanced hydraulic/hydrologic engineering techniques, the analysis shall be made by a currently licensed state-registered professional engineer proficient in hydraulics/hydrology. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 20) 
Sec. 16-400. - Variances. 
(a)	The county engineering department may grant a variance from the requirements of this article if exceptional circumstances applicable to a site exist such that strict adherence to provisions of this article will result in unnecessary hardship and will not fulfill the intent of this article. 
(b)	The county engineering department may grant a variance from requirements of this article if the proposed development will not: 
(1)	Change the rate or volume of runoff significantly; 
(2)	Have a significant, negative impact on any wetland, watercourse or water body; or 
(3)	Contribute to degradation of water quality. 
(c)	Site plans and supporting documentation to show conformance with the requirements of this article shall be submitted in accordance with applicable provisions of the subdivision regulations and shall include: 
(1)	Evidence of conformance with the requirements of this article for grading and drainage system alteration or development. Grading plans shall illustrate existing and proposed contours to the one-foot interval. Golf courses and other open space areas shall be exempt from this requirement, but general grading plans shall be submitted. Related plans shall show locations of structures, roads, surface drainage, existing and proposed drainage conduits and proposed alterations to the existing site or facilities; 
(2)	A hydrologic engineering analysis of stormwater runoff under existing and proposed developed site conditions and a detailed evaluation of the projected effects on upstream and downstream properties within the affected drainage basin. This analysis shall include a determination of the culvert, floodplain and channel cross section area required to carry the affected stream at the 25- and 100-year flood stage levels. The requirements for a complete hydrologic study may be waived by the county engineer for any development where the site plan submitted illustrates existing or proposed improvements sufficient to ensure compliance with applicable provisions of this article; 
(3)	Delineation of the boundaries and contour elevations of the 100-year floodplain as represented on the county's flood hazard maps prepared by FEMA. The actual building site in relation to the 100-year floodplain boundaries shall be shown. Any structure located in the 100-year floodplain shall show the finished floor elevation of the first floor. The same information shall be indicated by the seller to the purchaser of each property so affected. The elevation contours representing the intermediate regional flood conditions shall be shown when they are located outside established ditch banks. A benchmark suitable for determining 100-year flood elevations shall be established and shown on the plan; and 
(4)	The projected sequence of work represented by the grading and drainage plans as related to other major items of construction. 
(d)	Upon development/project completion, location, size and invert elevations of pipe segments of the storm drainage system, of control weirs, and maximum water surface elevations in retention ponds shall be shown on the final plat for a subdivision, and on a final plat for other developments which shall be submitted to the county engineer. The professional engineer reviewing the construction shall provide a certification that the development is in substantial compliance with approved plans for the project. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 20) 
Sec. 16-401. - Plan approval process. 
(a)	Unless granted an exemption, any person planning a development shall submit to the county engineering department four copies of a drainage plan, prepared in accordance with this article for review and approval. 
(b)	The county engineer or his designee shall review the plan. 
(1)	The county engineer shall issue a decision approving, rejecting or conditionally approving the plan with modification. 
(2)	The county engineer's decision will be based on conformance with requirements included in the city drainage regulations. No plan shall be approved unless it conforms with the requirements included in this article. The county engineer may require such additional documents or other items necessary to make this determination. 
(3)	If rejected, changes, additional analysis or other information needed to approve the next submittal of the plan shall be identified. 
(c)	If the drainage plan involves any stormwater management facilities or land to be dedicated to public use, the drainage plan shall be submitted to the engineering department for review and approval. 
(d)	Approved plans shall be valid for one year from the date of approval. 
(1)	Extensions or renewals of plan approvals shall be granted by the county engineering department upon written request by the person responsible for the development activity. 
(2)	A stormwater management plan shall not be considered approved without the inclusion of an approval stamp with a signature and date on the plans from the county engineering department. The stamp of approval on the plans is solely an acknowledgement of satisfactory compliance with the requirements of these regulations. The approval stamp does not constitute a representation or warranty to the applicant or any other person concerning the safety, appropriateness or effectiveness of any provision, or omission from the stormwater management plan. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 21) 
Sec. 16-402. - Permit suspension and revocation. 
(a)	Any development-related (subdivision/utility/other) permit may be suspended or revoked if one or more of the following violations are committed: 
(1)	Violation of the conditions of the drainage plan approval; 
(2)	Construction is not in strict accordance with the intent of approved plans; 
(3)	Noncompliance with any correction notice or stop work order; or 
(4)	Existence of immediate danger in the downstream area, as judged by the county engineering department. 
(b)	If one or more of the above are found, a written notice of violations shall be served upon the owner or his authorized representative, and an immediate stop work order may be issued. 
(1)	The written notice shall set forth measures necessary to achieve compliance with the plan; and 
(2)	Correction of the violations must be started immediately, or the owner shall be deemed in violation of this article. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 22) 
Secs. 16-403—16-432. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - STANDARDS AND SPECIFICATIONS 

Sec. 16-433. - County minimum requirements applicable. 
All engineering design items for storm drainage and erosion control and sedimentation control and delineation of the 100-year floodplains shall meet the applicable minimum requirements available from the county engineering department. Rainfall intensities used in hydrologic computations shall not be less than shown by applicable rainfall curves published by the National Weather Service for the affected area. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(1)) 
Sec. 16-434. - Combined storage and controlled release required for certain development. 
A combination of storage and controlled release of stormwater runoff shall be required for all development and construction which will increase the peak rate of runoff from the site by more than one cubic foot per second per acre for a 25-year frequency (type II) storm. This shall not apply to individual single-family lots of less than two acres. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(2)) 
Sec. 16-435. - Release rate. 
The release rate of stormwater from all developments where detention is required shall: 
(1)	Not exceed the peak stormwater runoff rate from the area in its existing state for all intensities up to and including the 25-year frequency for all durations of rainfall; or 
(2)	Not be greater than that calculated for a 25-year (type II) frequency storm with a runoff coefficient of 0.20, 0.25 and 0.35 for land with an average slope of up to two percent. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(3)) 
Sec. 16-436. - Adequate capacity required. 
The drainage system being developed shall have adequate capacity to accommodate the flow from all upstream areas for a type II storm of 25-year design frequency except for areas considered to be major drainage canals. The major drainage canals shall have adequate capacity to accommodate the flow from all upstream areas for a storm of 100-year frequency. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(4)) 
Sec. 16-437. - Impact of land use restricted. 
Land uses within the 100-year floodplain shall not diminish or restrict the capacity of the channels or floodplains of the stream, its tributaries, drainage ditches or any other drainage facilities or systems and shall not increase the 100-year elevation or velocity or concentration of flow in downstream areas. If the required hydrologic studies reveal that a request for filling or grading within the 100-year floodplain would overload the capacity of the channel downstream or increase flood stages upstream, the development permit shall be denied unless equivalent flow and storage capacity is replaced and maintained by the owner within the 100-year floodplain. Altered sections of the 100-year floodplain shall have a positive slope so as to provide positive drainage back to the stream flow line and this section must be maintained by the owners in perpetuity so as to prevent or remove silt build-up. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(5)) 
Sec. 16-438. - Live retention storage. 
The live retention storage to be provided shall be calculated on the basis of the 25-year frequency rainfall as published by the National Weather Service for the affected areas. The retention system required shall be that necessary to handle the runoff of a 25-year rainfall, for any and all durations from the proposed development, with a release rate that does not exceed the pre-development runoff. Retention control structures and other drainage improvements shall be located and designed to prevent erosion damage to adjacent property owners. Retention/detention control structures shall be sized for the release rate as presented in this article and will have provisions for overflow of the 100-year storm without damage to the structure. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(6)) 
Sec. 16-439. - Joint construction. 
When the developer requests and the county engineering department determines that development and construction projects are too small, or that engineering and economic factors make combined retention or other drainage facilities more practical, the city may authorize the joint construction of these facilities to serve two or more properties by two or more developers. This authorization shall be granted by the county engineering department upon application for approval being submitted through the planning commission. Where joint retention facilities serving two or more properties are approved for construction, no use of land or occupancy of buildings within the properties served by these facilities shall be permitted until completion of the retention facility, except upon approval of the county engineering department. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(7)) 
Sec. 16-440. - Available capacity. 
When adequacy of existing drainage structures are being considered in association with proposed development, the overall capacity of the structure will be evaluated and divided among upstream properties. The available capacity will be divided among property owners based on acreage in the basin. Under no condition will the available capacity of the structure be exceeded. Should the developer desire to replace the structure in lieu of retention/detention, all downstream structures should be evaluated and deemed adequate. The developer will be responsible for providing calculations and studies needed to evaluate downstream structures. If an existing structure not being modified by the development is found to be inadequate to handle the pre-development flows, the developer shall provide calculations to show the structure size required to handle the pre-development flows of the entire basin area. The city at that time will evaluate its ability to modify that structure. This evaluation will take into consideration available funds, required permits, capabilities of downstream structures and current workloads. Based on the county's findings, the developer will be notified within 45 days of the county's intentions for modification and any schedule required for modification of structures. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(8)) 
Sec. 16-441. - Installation, development, and maintenance. 
The following requirements shall apply to the installation, development and maintenance of all retention, detention and sedimentation control facilities designed for temporary storage of stormwater runoff: 
(1)	Permanent chainlink fencing at least six feet in height shall be required around all these facilities. This fencing shall be designed, installed and maintained to allow the free flow of runoff and sediment (if intended) into the facility. The fence shall include a lockable gate of sufficient size (12-foot minimum) to permit entrance of equipment necessary to allow periodic maintenance activities. Different fencing material may be substituted for chain link upon approval of the county engineering department. Requirements for fencing may be waived if deemed necessary by the city council. 
(2)	These facilities shall be located on tracts of land designated for this use on the recorded plat, with sufficient area around the perimeter to provide access for maintenance purposes and shall be immediately adjacent to or be provided with an access easement to a public street. The access easement shall provide at least 20 feet of width outside of aboveground obstructions including trees, utility poles, fences, buildings, headwalls, weirs, settling basins, top of slope or other drainage structures. 
(3)	Perforated standpipes or a French drain, as approved by the county engineer, or other methods which will achieve equal performance to prevent standing of water and/or inadequate drainage shall be installed within all these facilities. 
(4)	Except as provided in subsection (5) of this section the property owner shall be responsible for the maintenance of these retention facilities during grading, construction and following final approval of the completed project. This maintenance obligation shall be binding on future owners, successors and assigns of the property. 
(5)	In the case of single-family residential subdivisions approved after the date of adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived, the city shall assume maintenance responsibility two years after the release of subdivision streets. A special drainage district as authorized by O.C.G.A. § 36-31-12 will be established for property in a single-family residential subdivision at the time the plat is finally recorded and will be so noted on the plat. Upon completion of developer maintenance, all detention ponds shall have a positive slope to the outlet in order to facilitate complete drainage. 
(6)	Those facilities in single-family residential subdivisions constructed under permits issued prior to the adoption of this article will not be accepted for the city maintenance unless individually approved and accepted by the city council and suitable access easements are provided. At the time the city council accepts a retention facility for city maintenance, a special drainage district may be established that includes all properties for which the retention facility is designed. 
(7)	Pursuant to the creation of special drainage districts by the city as authorized by O.C.G.A. § 36-31-12, revenues to fund city maintenance of retention facilities may be obtained by an ad valorem tax on all properties for which the retention facilities are designed. Such ad valorem millage rates may be set annually by the LCPC when other ad valorem millage rates are set. No assessment will be made in a special drainage district in the calendar year in which it is established. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(9)) 
Sec. 16-442. - Drainage plan. 
Items required to be included in the drainage plan: 
(1)	A vicinity map with an indicating north arrow, scale, boundary lines of site, the land lot and district numbers, and other information necessary to locate the development site. 
(2)	Existing and proposed topography of the development site. 
(3)	A description of all watercourses, waterbodies, and wetlands on or adjacent to the site or into which stormwater flows. 
(4)	A description of physical improvements on the site, including present development and proposed development. 
(5)	Proposed dimensions, elevations, characteristics of all stormwater management facilities. 
(6)	Location of BMPs for water quality control, including temporary and permanent vegetative and structural measures, processes, procedures, prohibitions on practices, and other management practices that prevent or reduce discharge of pollutants in stormwater runoff. 
(7)	Identification of all areas within the site which will be included in land-disturbing activities and the expected date final stabilization will be completed. 
(8)	The anticipated starting and completion dates of various stages of land-disturbing activities and the expected date final stabilization will be completed. 
(9)	A determination that no occupied first-floor elevation of any structure is below the 100-year flood elevation. 
(10)	The designation of all easements needed for inspection and maintenance of the drainage system and stormwater management facilities and BMPs. 
(11)	All engineering calculations needed to design the system and associated structures, including: 
a.	Pre- and post-development runoff flows velocities; 
b.	Peak rates of discharge; and 
c.	Inflow and outflow hydrograph of runoff at all existing and proposed points of discharge from the site. 
(12)	A description of site conditions around all points of surface water discharge. This description shall include, but not be limited to: 
a.	Vegetation; and 
b.	The method of flow conveyance from any land-disturbing activity. 
(13)	Construction and design details for structural controls. 
(14)	An assessment of activities, materials, and physical features of the proposed development that have a reasonable potential to contribute significant amounts of pollutants to stormwater. Any such activities, materials, or features must be addressed by the measures and controls subsequently described in other portions of the stormwater management plan. 
(15)	Inclusion in the hydrologic-hydraulic study of an analysis of all stormwater management facilities and all major portions of the conveyance system through the proposed development for design conditions and operating conditions reasonably expected during the life of that facility. 
(16)	If the plan and/or design report indicates there may be a drainage or flooding problem at the exit to the proposed development, the county engineering department may require the following: 
a.	Water surface profiles of pre- and post-development conditions for design storms; and 
b.	Elevations of all structures potentially damaged by design-year flows. 
(17)	Certification by the person responsible for the land-disturbing activity that the activity will be accomplished pursuant to the approved plan, and responsible personnel will be assigned to the project. 
(18)	The name, address and telephone number of the developer/owner. 
(19)	The name, address and telephone number of a 24-hour, local contact responsible for stormwater runoff controls. 
(20)	The following maintenance statement: 
Stormwater runoff control measures will be maintained at all times. Additional stormwater runoff control measures will be installed if deemed necessary by on-site inspection. 
(21)	All maps, drawings and supportive computations shall bear the signature/seal of a professional engineer. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(10)) 
Sec. 16-443. - County regulations applicable to 100-year floodplain. 
All buildings located adjacent to or in the 100-year floodplain shall be constructed in accordance with the county flood damage prevention regulations. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(11)) 
Sec. 16-444. - Special drainage system maintenance requirements. 
The following are special drainage system maintenance requirements: 
(1)	No impoundment of water which retains in excess of 0.5 acre feet of runoff shall be removed without first obtaining a development permit, which shall only be issued after competent engineering studies provided by the developer show that this removal will not adversely affect downstream properties. 
(2)	Trash, garbage, construction materials, construction by-products or other debris shall not be deposited in any part of the drainage system. 
(3)	No restrictions or barriers, including fences, may be placed in the drainage system without first obtaining a development permit. When on- or off-site debris has accumulated within a floodplain in such a manner as to interfere with the free flow of water so as to increase the risk of hazardous inundation of upstream properties adjacent to the floodplain, the city shall require the owner of the property where this debris was generated, if its source can be identified, to clear and remove the debris so as to permit the free flow of water. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(12)) 
Sec. 16-445. - Water system design and location to minimize flood damage. 
The following are water system design and location requirements to minimize flood damage: 
(1)	All new and replacement water supply systems shall be designed to minimize or eliminate infiltration of floodwaters into the system. 
(2)	All new and replacement sanitary sewage systems shall be designed to minimize or eliminate infiltration of floodwaters into the system and discharges from the system into floodwaters. 
(3)	All on-site waste disposal systems shall be located to avoid impairment to them or contamination from them during flooding. 
(4)	All subdivision proposals shall have public utilities and facilities such as sewer, gas, electrical and water systems located and constructed to minimize flood damage. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 30(13)—(16)) 
Sec. 16-446. - Off-site drainage facilities. 
(a)	The county engineering department may allow stormwater runoff that otherwise is of unacceptable quality or which would be discharged in volumes or at rates in excess of those otherwise allowed by this article, to be discharged into drainage facilities off site of the development, provided the applicant has demonstrated: 
(1)	Off-site drainage facilities and channels leading to them are designed, constructed and maintained in accordance with requirements of this article; 
(2)	Adequate provision is made for sharing of construction, maintenance and operating costs of facilities. The developer may be required to pay a portion of the cost of constructing facilities as a condition to receiving approval of the drainage plan; and 
(3)	It is not feasible to completely manage runoff on site in a manner that meets the design and performance standards found in this article. 
(b)	A request to use off-site drainage facilities and all information related to proposed off-site facilities should be made a part of the developer's drainage plan. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 31) 
Sec. 16-447. - Reserved. 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2015-1, § I(6.5-32), adopted Sept. 1, 2015, repealed former § 16-447, which pertained to prohibitions, exemptions and illicit connections, and derived from an ordinance adopted Feb. 4, 1997, § 32. See Ch. 16, Art. III, Div. 3. 
Secs. 16-448—16-477. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 16-478. - Administration. 
(a)	The county engineering department will administer and enforce the provisions of this article. 
(b)	The county engineering department shall: 
(1)	Review all development permits to ensure that the permit requirements of this article have been satisfied; 
(2)	Advise permittee when additional federal or state permits may be required and, if specific federal or state permits are known to be required, ensure that copies of such permits are provided and maintained on file with the development permit; 
(3)	Notify adjacent communities, the Federal Emergency Management Agency and the state department of natural resources prior to any alteration or relocation of a watercourse and submit evidence of such notification to the Federal Insurance Administration; 
(4)	Administer, coordinate and oversee acquisition, design, construction, and operations and maintenance (O and M) of municipal/county stormwater facilities and conveyances; 
(5)	Establish or oversee establishment of development standards and guidelines; 
(6)	Determine the manner in which stormwater facilities should be operated; 
(7)	Inspect private systems which discharge to the county and city storm sewer systems; 
(8)	Advise the city and other departments on issues related to stormwater; 
(9)	Protect facilities and properties controlled by the city and prescribe how they are used by others; 
(10)	Require new, increased, or significantly changed stormwater contributions to comply with the terms of this article; 
(11)	Develop programs or procedures to control the discharge of pollutants into the city storm sewer system. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 40(1)) 
Sec. 16-479. - Enforcement. 
The county engineer or his representative shall administer and enforce those provisions of this article which apply to developed and occupied areas and to undeveloped areas which affect the city's responsibility for maintenance of the storm drainage system. The county engineer shall ensure that any altered or relocated portion of any watercourse is maintained so that flood-carrying capacity is not diminished. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 40(2)) 
Sec. 16-480. - Flood hazard map preparation. 
The county engineer shall prepare and maintain the flood hazard map using the most current flood insurance study prepared by the Federal Emergency Management Agency with accompanying maps or by using engineering studies prepared under the supervision of a currently licensed state-registered professional engineer, who, by using common and appropriate engineering procedures, shall deem such studies accurate and acceptable for floodplain definition. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 41) 
Sec. 16-481. - Inspection and right-of-way. 
(a)	Upon presentation of identification to the developer, contractor, owner, owner's agent, operator or occupants, employees of the city may enter during all reasonable hours any property under proposed or existing development and construction. These employees may make inspections of the facilities for the purpose of determining plan requirements or compliance with the provisions of this article. 
(b)	Designees of the county engineer may inspect any drainage system within or outside of an existing drainage easement. All drainage facilities located on private property, whether dedicated to the city or not, shall be accessible at all times for city inspection. 
(c)	Where drainage facilities are accepted by the city for maintenance, public access easements shall be provided. Reasonable access shall be provided to all drainage easements for inspection and maintenance functions. 
(d)	Where an easement does not exist for the drainage system, the permission of the owner shall be obtained before entrance. However, in the event of emergency maintenance requirements, permission of the owner shall not be mandatory. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 42) 
Sec. 16-482. - Ownership, maintenance, and inspections. 
(a)	Any stormwater management facility which services a single lot or commercial and industrial development shall be privately owned and maintained. The owner shall maintain a perpetual, nonexclusive easement which allows for access for maintenance. 
(b)	All other stormwater management control facilities shall be publicly owned and/or maintained only if accepted for maintenance by the city. 
(c)	The county engineering department may require dedication of privately owned stormwater facilities which discharge to the city storm sewer system. 
(d)	The county engineering department shall determine inspection schedules necessary to enforce the provisions of this article. Inspections may include, but are not limited to, the following: 
(1)	An initial inspection prior to drainage plan approval; 
(2)	A bury inspection prior to burial of any underground drainage structure; 
(3)	Erosion control inspections as necessary to ensure effective control of erosion and sedimentation; and 
(4)	A final inspection when all work, including installation of drainage facilities, has been completed. 
(e)	The county engineer or his designee, bearing proper credentials and identification, shall be permitted to enter, in accordance with state and federal law, all properties for regular inspections, periodic investigations, observation, measurement, enforcement, sampling and testing, in accordance with provisions of this article. The engineer or his designee shall duly notify the owner of said property or the representative on site, except in the case of an emergency. 
(f)	The county engineer or designated employee of the city, bearing proper credentials and identification, shall be permitted to enter, in accordance with state and federal law, all properties for which the city holds a negotiated easement for repairs, maintenance and other purposes related to any portion of the stormwater management facilities lying within said easement. The county engineer or his designee shall duly notify the owner of said property or the representative on site, except in the case of an emergency. 
(g)	If, after inspection, the condition of a facility presents an immediate danger to the public health, safety or general welfare because of unsafe conditions or improper maintenance, the city shall have the right, but not the duty to take action as may be necessary to protect the public and make the facility safe. 
(h)	The county engineering department shall inspect the work and shall either approve it or notify the applicant in writing in what respects there has been failure to comply with the requirements of the approved drainage plan. Any portion of the work which does not comply shall be promptly corrected by the applicant, or said applicant shall be subject to a penalty. 
(i)	The county engineering department shall prepare an inventory of detention/retention structures located in the city that are installed after the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived. The structures on this list shall be inspected once per year to ensure proper maintenance. An annual report shall be given to the city stating the condition of detention/retention structures within the city limits. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 43) 
Sec. 16-483. - Emergency maintenance. 
(a)	The city may conduct emergency maintenance operation on private land and on drainage systems where emergency conditions exist. Emergency maintenance shall constitute the removal of trees and other debris, which in the judgment of the county engineer or his representative create a condition potentially injurious to life, property and the public road system. 
(b)	Emergency maintenance conducted on any drainage system shall not be construed as constituting a continuing maintenance obligation on the part of the city. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 44) 
Sec. 16-484. - Notice of violation/stop work order. 
(a)	Whenever the county engineer or his representative determines that activity on a property does not comply with the approved development and construction plans, he may issue a notice of violation and/or a stop work order. 
(b)	Whenever the county engineer determines that the drainage system has been unlawfully altered, causing inadequate drainage, he may issue a notice of violation and/or a stop work order. 
(c)	A stop work order or notice of violation of the provisions of this article or of any rule or regulation adopted pursuant thereto shall be directed to the owner of the property or his agent and shall: 
(1)	Be in writing; 
(2)	Include a description of the property sufficient to identify where the violation has occurred; 
(3)	State that, if repairs, construction or alterations are not completed within a reasonable time period specified by the inspector, summons shall be issued for the owner to appear in court. 
Each day the violation continues shall constitute a new and separate violation. However, in the judgment of the county engineer, where the violation is willful, in wanton disregard of the provisions of this article, or constitutes a public health and safety hazard, he may issue a court summons in lieu of a notice of violation. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 45) 
Sec. 16-485. - Administrative appeal. 
(a)	Any person aggrieved by a decision of the county engineering department (including any decision with reference to the granting or denial of a variance from the terms of this article) may appeal the same by filing a written notice of appeal with the county engineer within 15 days of the issuance of said decision by the engineer. 
(b)	The county engineer can then reverse his decision or send this notice to the LCPC. A notice of appeal shall state the specific reasons why the decision of the county engineer is alleged to be in error, and the county engineer shall prepare and send to the LCPC and appellant a written response to said notice of appeal within 30 days of receipt of the notice of appeal. 
(c)	The LCPC will then make a recommendation to the city with regards to the appeal. The city will make the final decision regarding the appeal. 
(d)	All appeals shall be heard by the city council in accordance with city bylaws. The hearing shall be held within 60 days after receipt of notice of appeal or a date mutually agreed upon in writing by the appellant and the chairperson of the city council. The city council shall then make its findings within 30 days of the appeal hearing. Decisions of the city council shall be based on guidelines for appeals established by the city council and amended from time to time, with guidelines published in a newspaper of general circulation. 
(e)	If the appellant is dissatisfied with the city council decision, he can appeal said decision to the county court of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 46) 
Sec. 16-486. - Civil penalties. 
Any person violating any provision of this article, permitting conditions, or stop work order shall be liable for a civil penalty of not less that $100.00 per day or more than $500.00 per day, by a sentence of imprisonment not exceeding 60 days in jail, or both fine and jail. Each day the violation continues shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 47) 
Sec. 16-487. - Legal status provisions. 
The provisions of this article shall apply to all development activity within the city. The provisions shall not, however, be construed as repealing or modifying any condition attached to the issuance of any development permit issued prior to the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived. Further, this article shall not be construed so as to require any department of the city government to amend any development permit issued prior to the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived. However, the standards set forth in this article shall apply to all development, as defined in section 16-375, subsequent to the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 48) 
Sec. 16-488. - Cooperation with other governments. 
The city may enter into agreements with other local governments to carry out the purpose of this article. These agreements may include, but are not limited to, enforcement of provisions, resolution of disputes, cooperative monitoring and cooperative management of stormwater system and management programs. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 49) 
Sec. 16-489. - Property owner liability; supplemental charges. 
Any person in violation of any portion of this article shall pay for all costs to the city associated with the violation, including, but not limited to, containment, cleanup, injury, death, legal and other costs. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1997, § 50) 
Secs. 16-490—16-516. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - WELLHEAD PROTECTION 

Sec. 16-517. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this article is to ensure the provision of a safe and sanitary drinking water supply for the city by the establishment of wellhead protection zones surrounding the wellheads for all wells which are the supply sources for the city water system and by the designation and regulation of property uses and conditions which may be maintained within such zones. 
(Ord. of 12-11-1996, § 1) 
Sec. 16-518. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Hazardous waste or material means any waste or material which because of its quantity, concentration or physical, chemical or infectious characteristics may: 
(1)	Cause or significantly contribute to an increase in mortality or an increase in serious irreversible or incapacitating reversible illness; or 
(2)	Pose a substantial present or potential hazard to human health or to the environment when improperly treated, stored, transported, disposed of or otherwise managed. 
Sanitary landfill means a disposal site where solid wastes, including putrescible wastes, are disposed of on land by placing earth cover thereon. 
Wellhead means the upper terminal of a well, including adapters, ports, seals, valves and other attachments. 
(Ord. of 12-11-1996, § 2) 
Sec. 16-519. - Establishment of wellhead protection zone. 
There is hereby established a use district to be known as a wellhead protection zone, identified and described as all the area within a circle, the center of which is the center of any city water supply wellhead and the radius of which is 100 feet. 
(Ord. of 12-11-1996, § 3) 
Sec. 16-520. - Permitted uses. 
The following uses shall be permitted within wellhead protection zones: 
(1)	Any use permitted within existing agricultural or single-family residential districts, except that the minimum residential lot size for a lot any portion of which lies within the wellhead protection zone shall not be less one acre; and 
(2)	Any other open land use where any building located on the property is incidental and accessory to the primary open land use. 
(Ord. of 12-11-1996, § 4) 
Sec. 16-521. - Prohibited uses. 
The following uses or conditions shall be and are hereby prohibited within wellhead protection zones, whether or not such use or condition may otherwise be ordinarily included as a part of a use permitted under section 16-520: 
(1)	Surface use or storage of hazardous material, expressly including commercial use of agricultural pesticides; 
(2)	Septic tanks or drain fields appurtenant thereto; 
(3)	Impervious surfaces other than roofs of buildings, streets, driveways and walks serving buildings permitted under section 16-520; 
(4)	Sanitary landfills; 
(5)	Hazardous waste disposal sites; 
(6)	Stormwater infiltration basins; 
(7)	Underground storage tanks; 
(8)	Sanitary sewer lines within 150 feet of a wellhead. 
(Ord. of 12-11-1996, § 5) 
Sec. 16-522. - Administration. 
The policies and procedures for administration of any wellhead protection zone established under this article, including without limitation those applicable to nonconforming uses, exceptions, enforcement and penalties, shall be the same as provided in existing zoning regulations for the city, as the same are presently enacted or may from time to time be amended. 
(Ord. of 12-11-1996, § 6) 
Secs. 16-523—16-552. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - WETLAND PROTECTION 

Sec. 16-553. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Jurisdictional wetlands means an area that meets the definitional requirements for wetlands as determined by the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers. 
Jurisdictional wetlands determination means a delineation of jurisdictional wetlands boundaries by the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers, as required by section 404 of the Clean Water Act, 33 USC 1344, as amended. 
Regulated activity means any activity, which will, or which may reasonably be expected to result in the discharge of dredged or fill material into waters of the United States excepting those activities exempted in section 404 of the Federal Clean Water Act. 
Wetland means an area that is inundated or saturated by surface water or groundwater at a frequency and duration sufficient to support, and under normal circumstances does support, a prevalence of vegetation typically adapted for life in saturated soil conditions, commonly known as hydrophilic vegetation. Wetlands generally include swamps, marshes, bogs, and similar areas. 
Wetlands map means the current U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service national Wetlands Inventory Maps for the City of Riceboro, Georgia. 
Wetlands protection district means all wetlands within the jurisdiction of the city as indicated on the wetlands map; provided, however, that the wetlands map does not necessarily represent the boundaries of jurisdictional wetlands within the city and cannot serve as a substitute for a delineation of wetland boundaries by the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers as required by section 404 of the Clean Water Act, as amended (Federal Water Pollution Control Act, 33 USC 1251 et seq.). Any local government action under this article does not relieve the landowner from federal or state permitting requirements. 
(Ord. of 4-3-2001, § 5-100) 
Sec. 16-554. - Permitting determination. 
(a)	The Liberty Consolidated Planning Commission (LCPC) shall compare proposals for land disturbance or development with the generalized wetlands map and decide whether local permitting should proceed or be deferred pending U.S. Army Corps of Engineers determination. 
(b)	Upon review of project proposals or plans submitted, one of two actions should result: 
(1)	A local permit is issued without requiring jurisdictional wetlands determination by the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers. This action should be taken when the activity being proposed meets either of the following tests: 
a.	It is not the type of activity that would cause the alteration of wetlands; or 
b.	The proposed location of the activity is not near or within a protected wetland boundary as shown on the generalized wetlands map adopted by the local government. 
(2)	The local permit is deferred pending a jurisdictional wetlands determination by the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers. This action should be taken when the activity being proposed fails both of the above tests (i.e., it is a type of activity that would cause alteration of wetlands and the proposed location of the activity is near or within a wetland boundary). In this case, the local permit is issued only after a letter of permission or section 404 Permit is obtained from the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers. 
(Ord. of 4-3-2001, § 5-101) 
Secs. 16-555—16-573. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - LANDSCAPE AND TREE PROTECTION 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 16-574. - Purpose. 
The purposes of this article are to: 
(1)	Protect and maintain the urban forest by managing the impact of development. 
(2)	Preserve the environment and aesthetic assets of the community by requiring tree planting and landscaping for development. 
(3)	Provide protection from removal for all trees without a permit within the areas covered by this article unless exempted. 
(4)	Maintain where possible a minimum 50-percent canopy tree cover across the city. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-104) 
Sec. 16-575. - Exemptions. 
The following developments are exempted from compliance with the permitting requirements of this article: 
(1)	Utility easements for power lines, pipelines, or similar facilities, except where such utilities cross tree easements, set-asides, or natural buffers. 
(2)	Those portions of airport and heliports which require clear areas for safety purposes, including runways and taxiways, approach and departure clear zones. 
(3)	Land currently zoned and used for agricultural or other rural residential zoned purposes for the duration of such use, provided that such lands are not located within the jurisdiction of the city. In these cases, a 30-foot dense vegetative buffer shall remain around the perimeter of the site to prevent the site from being an eyesore. 
(4)	All activities excepted by O.C.G.A. § 12-7-17. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-105) 
Sec. 16-576. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
50 percent cover means a canopy expected to be achieved over a 30-year period by the planting of large, preferred trees or the retention of existing canopied trees which result in a minimum of 50 percent cover across the county. Fifty percent canopy cover will be approximately 18 large, preferred trees per acre, quantified as 1,600 tree quality points per acre. 
Administrator means the director of the Liberty Consolidated Planning Commission (LCPC) or designee. 
Buffer means any visual and physical separation between two parcels of land. 
Caliper means the diameter or thickness of the main stem of a young tree or sapling as measured at six inches above ground level. This measurement is used for nursery-grown trees having a diameter of four inches or less. 
Canopy trees means large preferred trees which provide canopy over streets and sidewalks and other paved areas. Upon reaching maturity, a canopy tree will achieve a canopy spread of in excess of 40 feet in diameter. Using a radius of 20 feet for calculation purposes, the canopy cover area for one mature tree will be equal to 3.1416 by 20 squared or 1,257 square feet. Total canopy coverage for one acre of land would be equal to 43,560 divided by 1,257 which equals 35 large canopy trees. 
Critical root zone means the minimum area surrounding a tree that is considered essential to support the viability of the tree and is for purposes of this article equal to the diameter at breast height (DBH) in inches converted into the radius of the circular area in feet around a preserved tree. 
Developable acres means the land area that can potentially be developed; i.e., this area does not include environmentally sensitive areas including, but not limited to, wetlands, stream buffers, marshlands, etc. 
Development means the act, process, or state of erecting buildings or structures, or making improvements to a parcel or tract of land. 
Diameter breast height (DBH) means the diameter or width of the main stem of a tree as measured 4.5 feet above the natural grade at its base. Whenever a branch, limb, defect, or abnormal swelling of the trunk occurs at this height, the DBH shall be measured at the nearest point above or below 4.5 feet at which a normal diameter occurs. 
Exceptional tree means any tree designated, as provided for in this article, to be of notable historic interest, aesthetic value, or of unique character because of species, type, age or size. 
Greenspace means any area retained as permeable unpaved ground and dedicated on the site plan to supporting vegetation. 
Greenspace plan means a map and/or supporting documentation which describes for a particular site where vegetation (greenspace) is to be retained or planted in compliance with these regulations. The greenspace plan shall include a tree survey, tree establishment plan, and/or a tree protection plan, and a landscape plan. 
Landscape plan means a map and supporting documentation which describes for a particular site where vegetation is to be retained or provided in compliance with the requirements of this article. The landscape plan shall include any required buffer elements. 
Landscape quality point (LQP) means a unit of measurement which quantifies the relative value of small trees, shrubs, and ground cover which are planted or retained on a given site. 
Native tree means any tree species which occurs naturally and is indigenous within the region. 
Plot plan means a map and supporting documentation which describes for a particular site where the buildings, driveway, utility corridors, and easements are to be located and where greenspace is to be retained or planted in compliance with these regulations. 
Preliminary plan means a plan which shows the proposed design for a commercial project or subdivision as specified in the subdivision regulations. 
Quality points factor means a decimal fraction that is assigned to each tree species in the tree lists and is used as a multiplier in calculating the tree quality points for any tree retained on a site. 
Set-asides means a piece of land dedicated to open space by the developer or owner. Examples of set-asides include parklands, recreation areas, medians of boulevards, etc. 
Sketch plan means a conceptual layout for a subdivision as specified in the subdivision regulations. 
Species diversity means a planting or retention of diverse tree species on a site or within the community to prevent dominance by any single type of tree. The purpose of this diversity is to prevent the destruction of the entire urban forest in the event of disease or pestilence. For any site of one acre or larger, no more than 45 percent of trees and shrubs planted shall be of the same species. 
Tree easement means an easement not less than ten feet in width and not in conflict with any other planning requirements under the zoning and subdivision regulations for public planting and/or maintenance of canopy street trees exclusive of utility, drainage, or other easements. Administrative approval is required for easements greater than ten feet in width. 
Tree establishment plan means a map and supporting documentation which describes for a particular site where existing trees are to be planted in compliance with the requirements of these regulations, the types of trees and their corresponding tree quality points. 
Tree fund means the tree protection escrow fund established to receive funds paid in lieu of required tree quality points or for compensation for damage or removal of trees owned by the governing authority. 
Tree protection plan means a map and surrounding documentation which describes for a particular site where existing trees are to be retained in compliance with the requirements of these regulations, the types of trees, and their corresponding tree quality points. 
Tree protection zone means the area surrounding a preserved or planted tree that is essential to that tree's health and survival, and is protected within the guidelines of these regulations. The minimum tree protection zone required for retained trees is the tree diameter's inches (DBH) converted into feet of radius around the tree. For planted trees, see table. 
Tree quality point (TQP) means a unit of measurement which quantifies the relative value of trees that are planted or retained on a given site. Tree quality points quantitatively express the desirable qualities of the species with regards to size for each tree that is retained on a site. For planted trees, tree quality points are an expression of species desirability and the expected mature size of each tree. 
Tree survey means a map or site plan prepared and sealed by a registered land surveyor within two years of the date of application. The survey shall be at the same scale as the required site development plan and shall include the following information: the location of all trees 16 inches or greater within the limits of disturbance and 25 feet beyond in each direction or to the property line whichever is less. 
Used for shall include the phrases "arranged for," "designed for," "intended for," and "occupied for." 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-106) 
Sec. 16-577. - Penalties for violation. 
Violation of the provisions of this article or failure to comply with any of its requirements, including violation of conditions and safeguards established in connection with grants of variance shall constitute a violation of this article. Any person who violates this article or fails to comply with any of its requirements shall, upon conviction thereof, be punished in accordance with section 1-11 and, in addition, shall pay all costs and expenses involved in the case. Each day such violation continues shall be considered a separate offense. Nothing contained in this article shall prevent the city from taking such other lawful action as is necessary to prevent or remedy any violation. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-117) 
Sec. 16-578. - Variance and appeal procedure. 
(a)	Appeals from decisions of the administrator or requests for variances from the provisions of this article shall be made to the LCPC which shall formulate a recommendation to the city. 
(b)	A variance shall be granted only: 
(1)	Upon a determination that the request is the minimum necessary to afford relief and that the overall intent and purpose of this article will not be adversely impacted; and 
(2)	Upon showing of good and sufficient cause. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-115) 
Sec. 16-579. - Notice of violation; remediation and stop work. 
(a)	Notice of violation. Whenever it is determined that a violation of this article has occurred, the administrator shall immediately issue a written notice to the person in violation, identifying the nature and location of the violation and specifying the remedial action that is necessary to bring the violation into compliance. The person in violation shall immediately commence remedial action and shall have seven calendar days after the receipt of the notice or such longer time as may be specified in the notice to complete the remedial actions required to bring the activity into compliance with this order. 
(b)	Stop work order. The administrator shall have the authority to immediately issue a stop work order in any of the following circumstances: 
(1)	When clearing or other development of land is being implemented without an approved permit. 
(2)	When ongoing noncomplying work is not immediately and permanently stopped upon receipt of a written notice of violation. 
(3)	When tree protection measures have not been implemented or maintained and danger to protected trees exists or appears imminent. 
(4)	When remedial work required by notice of violation is not completed within the time period specified. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-116) 
Sec. 16-580. - Abrogation and greater restrictions. 
This article is not intended to repeal, abrogate, or impair any existing easements, covenants, or deed restrictions. However, where this article and another conflict or overlap, whichever imposes the more stringent restrictions shall prevail. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-118) 
Sec. 16-581. - General provisions. 
(a)	Administration. The director of the Liberty Consolidated Planning Commission (LCPC) or the designee of the city shall administer the provisions of this article. 
(b)	Permit required for clearing. Except as provided in this article, a property owner shall not clear or permit the clearing of property or the removal of any tree without first obtaining a clearing permit as provided for in division 7 of this article. 
(c)	Protected trees. The following trees are protected within the jurisdiction of the governing authority and shall not be removed unless a permit has been approved or the requirement waived: 
(1)	On undeveloped property, any tree greater than two inches DBH. 
(2)	On developed property, any tree equal to or greater than two inches DBH except for single-family residential lots within a common development (subdivision) and exemptions defined in subsection (c)(2)d. 
a.	Any tree retained for the purpose of tree quality points or greenspace requirements. 
b.	Any tree planted for the purpose of tree quality points. 
c.	Any tree in a wetland, except as defined in the exemptions in subsection (c)(2)d of this section. 
d.	Any tree designated as an "exceptional tree." 
(d)	Tree/landscape quality points required. 
(1)	A total of not less than 1,600 tree quality points per developable acre is required for any parcel of land being developed (with the exception of single- family residential lots) and may include existing trees retained and new trees planted. 
(2)	A total of 400 landscape quality points per developable acre is required for commercial, industrial, institutional, or multifamily developments. 
(3)	A total of 1,200 tree quality points per acre is required for any parking area included in a commercial, industrial, institutional, or multifamily development. 
(4)	Any previously developed site that is proposed for redevelopment, building addition or other improvements requiring submittal of a site plan shall comply with the tree quality and landscape quality points requirements for that portion of the site affected by the redevelopment, addition, or improvement. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-107(a)—(d)) 
Sec. 16-582. - Landscape and tree ordinance manual. 
The landscape and tree ordinance manual and implementation guide is hereby adopted by reference. All land-clearing, tree protection, tree establishment, and landscaping shall be done in a manner consistent with the provisions contained in said manual. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-107(6)) 
Sec. 16-583. - Establishment of a tree fund. 
There is hereby created a tree protection escrow fund for the purpose of receiving money paid to the in-lieu-of required tree quality points, or for compensation for damage or removal of trees owned by the governing authority. The fund will be used by the LCPC to plant trees or landscaping on public rights-of-way, easements, or other public property. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-107(7)) 
Sec. 16-584. - Designation of an exceptional tree. 
A tree may be designated as an "exceptional tree" and will thereafter be considered a public landmark and shall not be destroyed or endangered. 
(1)	Procedure for designation as an exceptional tree. A tree may be nominated by written request to the administrator or may be nominated by the administrator. The nomination will be reviewed by the LCPC and a recommendation made to the city. 
(2)	Criteria. The designation of an exceptional tree shall be based upon evaluation of the tree in relation to one or more of the following criteria: 
a.	The tree is demonstrated to have an association with a documented historical event, or is located on a historic site. 
b.	The tree has unusually high aesthetic value. 
c.	The tree is of unique character because of its age, species, variety, location, or because of the size and development of its crown, trunk, or main stem. 
d.	The designation of an exceptional tree shall also meet all of the following criteria: 
1.	The tree is free of disease, pests, and other serious injury; 
2.	The tree has a life expectancy of more than ten years; 
3.	The tree is free from structural defects which would present a hazard to the public. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-107(8)) 
Secs. 16-585—16-601. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - TREE PROTECTION REQUIREMENTS AND TREE ESTABLISHMENT 

Sec. 16-602. - Protection of preserved or planted trees. 
Tree protection zones shall be established and maintained on the site for all trees, preserved or planted, for which tree quality points are to be claimed. The provisions of this division apply to such zones and the trees within them. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(a)) 
Sec. 16-603. - Tree protection plan. 
A tree protection plan and details shall accompany all applications for the land-clearing and/or land-disturbing activities identifying where and how existing trees are to be protected during clearing and construction of the project. Such plan and details shall be approved by the administrator upon a finding that the plan adequately addresses the criteria set forth in the landscape and tree ordinance manual. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(a)(1)) 
Sec. 16-604. - Tree protection zone. 
(a)	The minimum dimension of the tree protection zone shall be the area of the critical root zone. The tree protection zone shall be surrounded at a minimum by four-foot temporary chainlink fencing as illustrated in the specifications and standards in the landscape and tree ordinance manual. 
(b)	For planted trees, the following tree protection standards and requirements shall apply: 
MINIMUM TREE PROTECTION ZONE 

 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(a)(2), (a)(11)) 
Sec. 16-605. - Contingency planting plan. 
If a determination is made by the administrator that 75 percent of the tree quality points for a site are to be provided by one or more mature trees of greater than 30-inch DBH, a contingency planting plan shall be required. The contingency plan will include locations where trees can be planted for tree quality points (TQPs) credit in the event of the loss of retained trees. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(a)(3)) 
Sec. 16-606. - Water infiltration requirement. 
The area within any tree protection zone must remain open and unpaved. The use of perforated pavers or other surface allowing water infiltration may be allowed subject to the approval of the administrator. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(a)(4)) 
Sec. 16-607. - Restrictions and prohibitions. 
(a)	No root raking shall be allowed within any tree protection zone at any time during clearing, grading, or construction of the project. 
(b)	No trenching shall be allowed within any tree protection zone at any time during clearing, grading or construction of the project. 
(c)	No vehicle shall be parked, or construction material stored, or substances poured or disposed of or placed within any tree protection zone at any time during clearing, grading or construction of the project. 
(d)	No change in grade within the tree protection zone shall be allowed around existing trees except for a maximum addition of two inches of mulch unless approved by the administrator. 
(e)	To the extent possible, all site work shall be planned and conducted in a manner that will minimize damage to protected trees from environmental changes such as lowered water table, altered site drainage, or any other land disturbance within or immediately adjacent to the critical root zone of the trees. 
(f)	Tree wells or tree walls (islands) shall be constructed as needed to protect preserved trees from grade changes which result in changes of water supply to the tree protection zone. Adequate means for drainage of excess moisture from the tree protection zone shall be provided if tree wells or tree walls are constructed. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(a)(5)—(8)) 
Sec. 16-608. - Planting restrictions. 
(a)	No tree shall be planted closer to a building foundation, underground utility line, or storm drain as follows: 
(1)	Five feet for a small trees. 
(2)	Ten feet for a mature medium tree. 
(3)	Ten feet for a large tree; however, the distance from building foundations shall be 15 feet. 
(b)	No large or medium tree species shall be planted within any power or utility easements or under overhead utility distribution lines if the average mature height of the tree is greater than the lowest overhead wire. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(b)) 
Sec. 16-609. - Irrigation requirements. 
Except as provided for herein, irrigation shall be provided for tree protection zones in the following manner: 
(1)	All trees and landscaped areas shall be provided with a means for delivery of water in a quantity that is sufficient to establish and maintain the viability of the plants. A permanent water source shall be installed not less than 100 feet from each tree protection zone, but shall not encroach more than 12 inches into any tree protection zone. The minimum permanent water source permissible under these provisions shall be a hose bib capable of delivering a minimum of three gallons/minute. 
(2)	In-ground irrigation systems installed which supply water to all newly planted trees and plant material shall result in a 20-percent reduction of the landscape establishment bond. 
(3)	A water supply is not required for areas of established trees and other vegetation that are retained for greenspace requirements or tree quality points, provided that site grading or development activities will not result in damage to said areas. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(c)) 
Sec. 16-610. - Protection of public trees adjacent to land-development activities. 
(a)	A property owner responsible for any land-disturbing activity within proximity to the critical root zone of a tree located on city/county property shall provide for the protection of such tree to the standards described in these regulations. All work on rights-of-way requires a permit. 
(b)	A property owner responsible for a land-disturbing activity that causes damage to a tree which affects the health or growth of such tree, or requires removal of such tree, shall compensate the city for such tree loss or damage as set forth in subsection (c) of this section. 
(c)	The administrator shall establish the tree quality points for the removed or damaged tree. The property owner responsible for the land-disturbing activity which caused the removal or damage to such tree shall compensate the city for such tree loss or damage under the following options, subject to the approval of the administrator: 
(1)	Plant or preserve additional trees on the development site that equal or exceed the value of tree quality points that were assessed for the removed or damaged tree. 
(2)	Plant trees on adjacent rights-of-way to equal or exceed the value of tree quality points that were assessed for the removed or damaged tree. 
(3)	Make payment to the tree fund that equals or exceeds the value of the tree quality points that were assessed for the removed or damaged tree. 
(4)	Meet any equivalent combination of the above as approved. 
(d)	Upon approval by the administrator of the method for compensating the city for the subject tree loss, the owner shall submit a revised tree protection and tree establishment plan which incorporated the approved tree compensation plan to the administrator for approval. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(d)) 
Sec. 16-611. - General protection of trees on city rights-of-way. 
(a)	Unless otherwise permitted by an applicable permit or license, no person shall trim, prune, or remove any tree on public property without procuring the written approval of the administrator. 
(b)	No person shall plant any tree or shrub on the right-of-way without written approval or without meeting the requirements for such planting published by the administrator. 
(c)	No person shall cause damage to trees on rights-of-way or other public property. Damage is defined as cutting, carving, attaching any rope, wires, nails, signs or other object to any such tree or allowing any harmful gas, liquid, or solid substance to contact any tree or to set fire or permit any fire to burn which may injure any portion of any tree or causing unnecessary harm to tree roots through construction activities, vehicle parking, or material storage. 
(d)	Any removal or damage to trees on rights-of-way is subject to compensation as provided in 16-610(b). 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(e)) 
Secs. 16-612—16-640. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - STANDARDS, SPECIFICATIONS, AND CALCULATION OF TREE QUALITY POINTS 

Sec. 16-641. - Planted trees. 
(a)	All large trees, except for conifers, must be at least 2½-inch caliper to qualify for tree quality points when planted on the site. 
(b)	All coniferous trees and all medium trees must be a minimum of two-inch caliper to qualify for tree/landscape quality points when planted on the site. 
(c)	All small trees must be a minimum of one-inch caliper to quality for tree quality points when planted on the site. 
(d)	For palms, two tree quality points will be assigned per foot of stem height up to ten feet, regardless of whether the tree is preserved or planted on the site. 
(e)	All planting of new trees shall be done in accordance with ANSI A-300-1995 or the most recent edition. 
(f)	All trees and plant materials shall conform to the most recent edition of the American Standard for Nursery Stock by the American Association of Nurserymen. 
(g)	A detailed list of qualifying species and their points is provided in the landscape and tree ordinance manual. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(f)(1)) 
Sec. 16-642. - Retained trees. 
(a)	All individual preserved trees must be at least four inches DBH, and have a form and structure that will support a viable mature tree to qualify for tree quality points. The tree quality points (TQPs) credit will at a minimum be equal to the points for a planted tree of the same species. 
(b)	Quality points from trees retained on the site are directly related to the tree species quality and tree protection zone that must be provided for the tree. Tree quality points are calculated by the formula as follows: 
(DBH) 2 × (Retention Points Factor) = Tree Quality Points 
(c)	The retention factor for each tree species can be found in the landscape and tree ordinance manual. 
(d)	Trees located on public rights-of-way which have a significant portion of canopy extending over a commercial property can be applied toward TQP as follows: 
TQP value of public trees x percentage of canopy encroachment = the point value 
(e)	Tree quality points and landscape quality points for retained stands of trees. The preservation of mature native stands of trees and understory vegetation may have the value of 1,600 tree quality points/acre and 400 landscape quality points/acre of preserved area, providing compliance with the following: 
(1)	The area proposed for preservation must be approved by the administrator and must have sufficient quantity, size, and quality of mature trees to warrant preservation. 
(2)	All existing vegetation shall be left within the preserved stand with the exception of hazardous trees. Thinning of tree stands will be allowed pursuant to an approved plan created under the supervision of a registered forester or certified arborist. No mechanical clearing of underbrush shall be allowed unless authorized by the administrator. 
(3)	The area shall be protected during the construction period using the same standards and specifications as required for a tree protection zone. 
(4)	The tree retention area shall be considered a set-aside and shall be shown within a permanent recorded tree conservation easement. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(f)(2)) 
Sec. 16-643. - Landscape material. 
(a)	Woody ornamental or native shrubs shall be a minimum of three-gallon container size, fully rooted, and appropriately sized to the container. Vines and ground cover material may be full one-gallon size. 
(b)	Small trees used for landscape quality points (LQPs) shall be a minimum of one-inch caliper. 
(c)	Qualified species and LQP values are listed in the landscape and tree ordinance manual. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-108(f)(3)) 
Secs. 16-644—16-674. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - TIMBER HARVESTING AND OTHER REMOVALS 

Sec. 16-675. - Applicability. 
All properties, other than those zoned and used for agricultural activities, which propose timber harvesting or clear cutting shall comply with the provisions in this division unless exempted by O.C.G.A. § 12-7-17. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-109(a)) 
Sec. 16-676. - Permit and plan required. 
(a)	Permit required for timber harvest. A land-clearing permit is required prior to the timber harvest. 
(b)	Plan required for timber harvest. A plan for development of the land and a harvest plan shall be reviewed and approved by the Liberty Consolidated Planning Commission (LCPC) prior to the issuance of a timber harvesting/land-clearing permit. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-109(b)(1), (2)) 
Sec. 16-677. - Reforestation and tree protection standards. 
A minimum of 1,600 tree quality points per developable acre shall remain on the parcel after the timber harvest utilizing one or more of the following methods: 
(1)	Residual stands of trees. Tree quality points may be given to residual stands of trees which are existing on the site and are protected during the harvesting process. 
(2)	Buffer areas. Tree quality points may be given to trees located within buffer areas. 
(3)	Reforestation areas. Where the site is to be used for continual timber growth or silviculture, such land shall be considered a reforestation area. In order to comply with the provisions of this section, a tree establishment plan shall be submitted. This shall consist of the establishment of native tree seedlings using traditional forestry methods and best management practices. A minimum of 600 seedlings per acre shall be planted on the site by the end of the first planting season following the timber harvest. A minimum survival rate of 350 trees per acre will be maintained after the first complete growing season. 
(4)	Tree establishment plan. If an insufficient number of tree quality points are left on the site following the timber harvest, a tree establishment plan shall be submitted to the administrator showing the location of the trees to be planted, their species, size, and tree quality point listing. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-109(b)(3)) 
Sec. 16-678. - Underbrushing procedures. 
The administrator may approve underbrushing and removal of trees or other vegetation up to two inches in diameter upon finding that sufficient tree cover exists such that the removal of such trees will not limit or prevent compliance with other requirements of this article. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-110) 
Secs. 16-679—16-699. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - GREENSPACES 

Sec. 16-700. - Greenspace standards for all proposed development; plan required. 
A greenspace plan shall be submitted for all commercial, industrial, or multifamily development. Such plans shall conform to the standards and requirements of these regulations and the following: 
(1)	A minimum of 20 percent of the total land area of the development shall be devoted to greenspace. 
(2)	Sidewalks, curbing, or any other paved or impermeable surfaces within the greenspace shall not count towards the 20-percent minimum greenspace requirement. 
(3)	For all sites of one acre or larger, no more than 45 percent of trees planted shall be of the same species in order to increase species diversity. 
(4)	Existing groups of trees shall be retained wherever possible. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-111(intro.)) 
Sec. 16-701. - Locations for planting/preserving trees and landscaping. 
Street trees may be preserved within the front yard development setback, provided they can be placed within a tree easement established pursuant to the subdivision regulations, and such tree does not conflict with any existing utility, drainage or other easements. Understory and canopy trees may also be preserved and/or planted in the front yard development setback area. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-111(b)) 
Sec. 16-702. - Parking areas. 
(a)	A minimum of 1,200 tree quality points per acre of the parking area in canopy trees shall be planted and/or preserved within landscaped islands and medians located between parking bays. Landscape quality points may also be planted in these areas. 
(b)	Canopy trees planted in parking islands shall have 400 square feet of unpaved soil for root development. The standard tree island shall be 20 feet by 20 feet; provided, however, that where the islands are an extension of a ten-foot wide landscape median, the islands may be reduced in width to 16 feet. Islands shall not be separated by more than 12 parking spaces, including the landscaped ends of the drive aisles. Islands shall be designated so as to minimize foot traffic across them. 
(c)	The parking island requirement may be altered to minimize conflicts with lighting or to accommodate innovative design, provided that total area of unpaved area and number of trees is maintained. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-111(c)) 
Sec. 16-703. - Buffers. 
Existing and/or planted canopy, understory trees, and planted evergreen shrubs may be incorporated into buffer areas. Such planting shall be credited for quality points provided that other standards and requirements of this article are met. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-111(d)) 
Sec. 16-704. - Landscaping standards. 
(a)	Landscape quality points requirement. The required 400 landscape quality points per acre shall be provided through the planting of small/medium trees, shrubs, vines, and/or ground cover. 
(b)	Locations for landscape quality points. Such plantings may be located in the following areas: 
(1)	Front yard development setback. 
(2)	Parking areas, islands, and medians. 
(3)	Buffers. 
(4)	Areas adjacent to buildings. 
(Ord. of 7-6-2010, § 5-111(e)) 
Sec. 16-705. - Special cases. 
(a)	Insufficient space for trees on site. If the required tree quality points cannot be met on site due to lot size and allowable building setback, trees shall be planted off site or payment made to the tree fund. Off-site planting location or payment must be approved by the administrator. 
(b)	Insufficient space for landscaping on site. If the required landscape quality points cannot be met on site due to lot size and allowable building setback, payment shall be made to the tree fund. 
(c)	Car/boat/trailer sales lots.
