ARTICLE II. - UTILITY TAXES 

Sec. 36-19. - Definitions. 
For purposes of this article, the term "utility" shall be defined as any company providing a useful service to the public, particularly the service of electric, power, gas, telephone, cable television, etc. 
(Ord. of 10-6-1992, § 2) 
Sec. 36-20. - Applicability; amount and due date of payments. 
(a)	Each utility company operating in the city shall pay a special tax in the amount of four percent of the gross sales to customers served within the corporate limits of the city for the preceding quarter. 
(b)	Each payment shall be due on or before the last day of the second month following the end of each calendar quarter and shall be based on recurring local service record revenues billed during such calendar quarter. 
(c)	Any amount of franchise fees paid by a utility company under a contract entered into with the city that is applicable to any period subsequent to October 6, 1992, shall be credited against the amounts imposed in subsection (a) of this section or by a subsequent ordinance. 
(Ord. of 10-6-1992, § 1) 
Chapter 38 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Motor vehicles and traffic, O.C.G.A. § 40-1-1 et seq.; uniform rules of the road, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-1 et seq.; off-road vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 40-7-1 et seq.; equipment and inspection of motor vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 40-8-1 et seq.; abandoned motor vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 40-11-1 et seq.; use of speed detection devices, O.C.G.A. § 40-14-2 et seq.; cities and counties authorized to enact ordinances for removal of vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-4. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 38-1. - Authority of law enforcement and fire department officials to enforce chapter. 
It shall be the duty of law enforcement officers authorized by the city to enforce all city traffic laws. In addition, officers of the fire department, when at the scene of a fire, may direct or assist law enforcement officers in directing traffic thereat or in the immediate vicinity. 
State Law reference— Authority to regulate traffic by means of police officers preserved, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371(a)(1); obedience to persons directing traffic required, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-2. 
Secs. 38-2—38-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TRAFFIC REGULATIONS 

Sec. 38-21. - Adoption of uniform rules of the road. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 40-6-370, the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 40-6-1 et seq., known as the uniform rules of the road, and the definitions contained in O.C.G.A. § 40-1-1, are hereby adopted as and for the traffic regulations of the city with like effect as if recited in this article. 
Sec. 38-22. - Parental responsibility. 
It shall be unlawful for the parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and custody of a minor under the age of 16 years to permit, whether knowingly or through ineffective control or supervision, such minor to violate any provision of this Code or state law regarding the operation of vehicles. 
Sec. 38-23. - Sale of vehicles on rights-of-way prohibited. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful to park or leave unattended on or within the right-of-way of any public road in the unincorporated areas of the city any used motor vehicle that is marked for sale or otherwise displayed for sale. A vehicle shall be considered to be displayed for sale when a reasonable person would perceive that the vehicle is for sale without having to inquire whether the vehicle is for sale. 
(b)	The law enforcement officials of the city are authorized and empowered to impound any vehicle found to be in violation of subsection (a) of this section. The owner of such vehicle shall be responsible for all expenses and charges incurred in the towing and storage of the vehicle. 
Secs. 38-24—38-49. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - SPEED REGULATION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Maximum speed limits, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-181; power of local authorities to alter speed limits, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-183. 

Sec. 38-50. - Speed detection device authorized. 
The law enforcement officers of the city are authorized to use speed detection devices as permitted by O.C.G.A. § 40-14-2. 
(Res. of 5-11-1992) 
State Law reference— Georgia Peace Officer Training Act, O.C.G.A. § 35-8-1 et seq.; authority for use or speed detection devices by local law enforcement officers, O.C.G.A. § 40-14-2; requirements that local government obtain state permit, O.C.G.A. § 40-14-2. 
Sec. 38-51. - Speed limits on system highways. 
The following speed zones are hereby established based on an engineering and traffic investigation as prescribed by law: 
SPEED ZONES ON SYSTEM HIGHWAYS 

 
(Ord. No. 071499, 8-25-1999) 
Sec. 38-52. - Reduction of speed when speed hazards exist. 
(a)	No person shall drive a vehicle on a street or highway at a speed greater than is reasonable and prudent under the existing conditions and with due regard for the actual and potential hazards that exist. In every event speed shall be so controlled as may be necessary to avoid colliding with any person, vehicle or other conveyance on or entering the street, road, highway or other avenues of travel, in compliance with legal requirements and the duty of all persons to use due care and caution. 
(b)	Where no speed hazards exist that require lower speed for compliance with subsection (a) of this section, the speed of any vehicle not less than the minimum limits or not in excess of the maximum limits or established as authorized herein, shall be lawful, but no speed in excess of the maximum limits specified in this section, or established as authorized by this section, shall be unlawful unless special hazards exist that might require lower speed for compliance with subsection (a) of this section. 
State Law reference— Alteration of speed limits by local authorities, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-183. 
Chapter 40 - UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Public utilities generally, O.C.G.A. § 46-1-1 et seq.; municipal home rule, O.C.G.A. § 36-35-1 et seq.; municipal utilities, O.C.G.A. § 36-34-5; Georgia Water Quality Control Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-5-20 et seq.; water resources, O.C.G.A. § 12-5-1 et seq.; public water systems, O.C.G.A. § 12-5-170 et seq.; water supply, O.C.G.A. § 12-5-470; sewage and waste disposal, O.C.G.A. § 12-5-29 et seq.; refusal by city or county to supply water because of indebtedness of prior owner, occupant, or lessee prohibited, and limited liens for unpaid utility charges, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-17. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 40-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) means the quantity of oxygen utilized in the biochemical oxidation of organic matter under EPA-approved laboratory procedures in five days at 20 degrees, expressed in milligrams per liter. 
Building drain means that part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system which receives the discharge from waste and other drainage pipes inside the walls of buildings and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning five feet outside the inner face of the building wall. 
Building sewer means the extension from the building drain to the public sewer or other place of disposal, also called house connection or service connection. 
Combined sewer means a sewer receiving both surface runoff and sewage. 
Completion of work means the concurrence of the following events: 
(1)	The work required by the construction contract shall have been completed; 
(2)	The owner shall provide the city with a certificate verifying that payment has been made for all labor and material employed in connection with the construction of the improvements and that the improvements have been constructed in accordance with the construction contract; and 
(3)	All appropriate governmental authorities have inspected and approved the improvements and the improvements are in operation. 
Construction contract means an agreement between the owner and the general contractor which shall be approved by the engineer and includes the following: 
(1)	The contract; 
(2)	The general conditions; 
(3)	Plans and specifications; 
(4)	All addenda (as defined in the general conditions) issued prior to the execution of the construction contract; 
(5)	All amendments to the construction contract signed by both parties; and 
(6)	All change orders (as defined in the general conditions) signed by both parties. 
Contractor means a person, approved by the city council and consulting engineer, engaged in actual sewer construction or extensions within the jurisdiction of the city. 
Customer means every person who is responsible for contracting (expressly or implicitly) with the city in obtaining, having, or using sewer connections with, or sewer tap to, the city sewer system and in obtaining, having, or using water and other related services furnished by the city for the purpose of disposing of wastewater and sewage through said system. Said terms shall include the occupants of each unit of a multiple-family dwelling unit building as a separate and distinct customer. 
Drawings means detailed drawings prepared by a registered professional engineer showing the proposed sewer improvements as supplemented by detailed specifications. 
Easement means an acquired legal right for the specific use of property owned by others. 
Engineer means the city's consulting engineer on sewer matters or its designated representatives. 
Floatable oil means oil, fat, or grease in a physical state such that it will separate by gravity from wastewater by treatment in an approved pretreatment facility. Wastewater shall be considered free of floatable oil if it is properly pretreated and the wastewater does not interfere with the collection system. 
Properly shredded garbage means the wastes from the preparation, cooking and dispensing of food that have been shredded to such degree that all particles will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in the public sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch in any dimension. 
Public sewer means a common sewer controlled by a governmental agency or public utility. 
Sanitary sewer means a sewer that carries liquid and water-carried wastes from residences, commercial buildings, industrial plants and institutions together with minor quantities of groundwaters, stormwaters and surface waters that are not intentionally admitted. 
Septic tank means a subsurface impervious tank designed to temporarily retain sewage or similar waterborne wastes together with: 
(1)	A sewer line constructed with solid pipe, with the joints sealed, connecting the impervious tank with a plumbing stub out; and 
(2)	A subsurface system of trenches, piping and other materials constructed to drain the clarified discharge from the tank and distribute it underground to be absorbed or filtered. 
Sewage means the spent water of a community. The equivalent term is wastewater. 
Sewage works (sewerage) means all facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing of sewage. 
Sewer means a pipe or conduit that carries wastewater. 
Sewer impact fee means the fee charged by the city to individuals for the privilege of connecting to any existing or future system operated by the city. 
Slug means any discharge of water or wastewater which in concentration of any given constituent or in quantity of flow exceeds for any period of duration longer than 15 minutes or more than five times the average 24-hour concentration of flows during normal operation and shall adversely affect the collection system or performance of the wastewater facilities. 
Storm drain (sometimes termed storm sewer) means a drain or sewer for conveying water, groundwater, subsurface water, or unpolluted water from any source and excluding sewage and industrial wastes other than unpolluted cooling water. 
Superintendent means the superintendent of public works or his authorized deputy, agent or representative. 
Suspended solids means total suspended matter that either floats on the surface of, or is in suspension in, water, wastewater or other liquids, and is removed by laboratory filtration as approved by the environmental protection agency and referred to as nonfilterable residue. 
Unpolluted water means water of quality equal to or better than the effluent criteria in effect, or water that would not cause violation of receiving water quality standards and would not be benefited by discharge to the sanitary sewers and wastewater treatment facilities provided. 
Wastewater means the spent water of a community. From the standpoint of source, it may be a combination of the liquid and water-carried wastes from residences, commercial buildings, industrial plants, and institutions, together with any groundwater, surface water and stormwater that may be present. 
Wastewater facilities means the structures, equipment, and processes required to collect, carry away, and treat domestic and industrial wastes and dispose of the effluent. 
Watercourse means a natural or artificial channel for the passage of water either continuously or intermittently. 
Work means: 
(1)	All of the labor and material necessary to produce the construction required by the plans and specifications and all materials and equipment incorporated or to be incorporated in such construction. 
(2)	All necessary off-site work required by other governmental authorities having jurisdiction of the construction and operation of a sewer system. 
(3)	Connecting and hooking-up of electric and other utilities. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § II; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 1, § II; Ord. of 10-6-2009, art. 2) 
Sec. 40-2. - Interference with or damage to public utilities. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person intentionally and without authority: 
(1)	To damage or destroy any meter, pipe, conduit, wire, line, post, lamp or other apparatus belonging to the city or a company engaged in the manufacture or sale of electricity, gas, water, telephone, or other public services; 
(2)	To prevent a meter from properly registering the quantity of such service supplied; 
(3)	To use or cause to be used without the consent of such company or the city any service manufactured, sold or distributed by such company or the city; or 
(4)	To interfere, in any way, with the proper action of such company or the city. 
(b)	Where there is no evidence to the contrary, the person performing any of the illegal acts referred to in subsection (a) of this section, or the person who, with knowledge of such violation, received the benefit of such service without proper charge as a result of such improper action, shall be presumed to be responsible for such acts of tampering or diversion. 
(Ord. of 10-6-1992, § 1.2) 
Secs. 40-3—40-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - WATER 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 40-23. - Purpose. 
It is the purpose of this article to set forth requirements for obtaining water service in the city and further to regulate the operation of any private system. This article also provides that the city may establish specific standards and requirements for the construction of all new or replacement water lines and any accessories or extensions thereto. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § I) 
Sec. 40-24. - City's access to premises. 
Duly authorized agents of the city shall have access at all hours to the premises of the consumer for the purpose of installing or removing city property, inspecting piping, reading and testing meters, and for any other purpose in connection with the water service in these facilities and enforcing the provisions of this article or any rules promulgated under the authority thereof. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(E); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Secs. 40-25—40-51. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - CONNECTIONS 

Sec. 40-52. - Limitations on private supply facilities. 
No person shall operate private facilities for water supply for consumption by humans when existing or new service is available within 200 feet of the facility to be served. The city may waive this requirement for good cause shown and the city's decision in the exercise of its legislative discretion shall be controlling. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(A); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Sec. 40-53. - Water taps; application required. 
Only authorized city employees may tap the water line. Water for the city system shall not be introduced into any premises without a written application having first been made to the city and approved by the mayor. No water line shall be tapped except by authorized employees. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(B); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Sec. 40-54. - Responsibility of property owner for costs of water service lines. 
The owner of the property to be served shall be responsible for the cost, installation and maintenance of the water service line from the facility to be served to a point where the service line ties into the city system, which includes any portions of the service line extending on to the public right-of-way or city easement. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(D); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Sec. 40-55. - City's responsibility and liability. 
(a)	The city shall run a service line from its distribution line to the property line where the distribution line exists or is to be constructed and runs immediately adjacent and parallel to the property to be served. No service charge, other than the connection fee referred to in subsection (b) of this section, shall be made for five-eighths-inch by three-fourths-inch meters. A proportionately greater charge than the connection fee in subsection (b) of this section will be made for meters of larger dimensions. 
(b)	The city may make connections to serve other properties not adjacent to its lines upon payment of reasonable costs for the extensions of its distribution lines as may be required to render such service. 
(c)	The city may install its meters at or near the property line or, at the city's option, on the consumer's property within three feet of the property line. 
(d)	The city reserves the right to refuse service unless the consumer's lines or piping are installed in such a manner as to prevent cross connections or backflows. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 4, § III) 
Sec. 40-56. - Unauthorized connections. 
No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any corrections with or opening into, use, or disturb any public water main or appurtenances thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the city. No connection shall be made except at wyes, manholes or connection points approved by the mayor. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(C); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Sec. 40-57. - Right of city to revoke permission to connect to water system. 
The city shall have the right for good cause shown to revoke or annul at any time any permit previously issued for the connection to any water lines, and no party shall have the right to claim damage as a result of such permit being revoked or annulled. The city reserves the right to disconnect and discontinue its service without notice for the following additional reasons: 
(1)	To prevent fraud or abuse. 
(2)	Consumer's willful disregard of the city's rules. 
(3)	Emergency repairs. 
(4)	Insufficiency of water supply due to circumstances beyond the city's control. 
(5)	Legal proceedings. 
(6)	Direction of public authorities. 
(7)	Strike, riot, flood, fire, or unavoidable accidents. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(F); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Sec. 40-58. - Cross connections prohibited. 
No person shall install or operate a cross connection between a private water facility and any system belonging to the city. All private water facilities shall be at all times kept separate and apart from the city systems. The separation of such a system by the placement of valves between facilities will not be allowed. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(J); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Sec. 40-59. - Stopcock or cutoff valve requirements. 
The following requirements shall apply to all water connections: 
(1)	A stopcock and wastecock or cutoff valve must be placed by the property owner on his property between the building and the meter and, if possible, within one or two feet of the meter. The cutoff valve will be under the control of the owner and will be used in case of an emergency, so that any pipe to be repaired can be cut off so as to avoid interference with the city system. 
(2)	The stopcock, box and meter at or near the property lines shall be the property of the city. The city stopcock will be used only by authorized city personnel. 
(3)	Where meters or meter boxes are placed on the premises of a consumer, a suitable place shall be provided by the consumer therefor, unobstructed and accessible at all times to the meter reader. 
(4)	The consumer's piping and apparatus shall be installed and maintained by the consumer at the consumer's expense in a safe and efficient manner and in accordance with the sanitary regulations of the state health department. 
(5)	The pipe from the main water line or meter to the served premises shall be the property of the owner, and all repairs to such lines shall be at the owner's expense. The city shall have an easement to use any portion of the pipe located off of city property and any land adjacent thereto so long as any service is provided to the premises by the city. 
(6)	All water service used in a fire protection system must comply with the following provisions: 
a.	The customer shall provide and maintain separate and independent plumbing facilities including a glob detector check valve or comparable equipment and shall maintain the sprinkler system in good working order. 
b.	A separate water supply shall be installed by the owner or occupant. Customers with a separate water supply for fire protection will be charged a monthly fee in accordance with a schedule of fees which shall include an estimated amount of water usage should the system be employed. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 3, § I) 
Sec. 40-60. - Private well connection prohibited. 
In order to be received as a consumer entitled to receive water from the city's water system, all applicants must offer proof that any private wells located on their property are not physically connected to the lines of the city's water system, and all applicants, by becoming consumers of the city, covenant and agree that so long as they continue to be consumers of the city, they will not permit the connection of any private wells on their property to the city's water system. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(K); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Sec. 40-61. - Connection in floodplain prohibited. 
The city will not allow any connection to any facility located in a 100-year floodplain as designated on the relevant flood maps published by the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA), within any jurisdictional freshwater wetlands, prime farmland, or endangered or threatened species habitat. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(L); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Secs. 40-62—40-80. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - FIXTURES 

Sec. 40-81. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Commercial means any type of building other than residential. 
Construction means the erection of a new building or the alteration of an existing building in connection with its repair or renovation or in connection with making an addition to an existing building and shall include the replacement of a malfunctioning, unserviceable, or obsolete faucet, showerhead, toilet, or urinal in an existing building. 
Residential means any building or unit of a building intended for occupancy as a dwelling but shall not include a hotel or motel. 
(Ord. of 6-9-1992, div. 7, § 1) 
Sec. 40-82. - Restrictions. 
(a)	No construction may be initiated within the city for any residential building of any type which: 
(1)	Employs a gravity tank-type, flushometer-valve, or flushometer-tank toilet that uses more than an average of 1.6 gallons of water per flush; provided, however, this subsection shall not be applicable to one-piece toilets; 
(2)	Employs a shower head that allows a flow of more than an average of 2.5 gallons of water per minute at 60 pounds per square inch of pressure; 
(3)	Employs a urinal that uses more than an average of 1.0 gallons of water per flush; 
(4)	Employs a lavatory faucet or lavatory replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than 2.0 gallons of water per minute; or 
(5)	Employs a kitchen faucet or kitchen replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than 2.5 gallons of water per minute. 
(b)	The requirements of subsection (a) of this section shall apply to any residential construction and to any commercial construction which involves the repair or renovation of or addition to any existing building when such repair or renovation of or addition to such existing building includes replacement of toilets or showers or both. 
(Ord. of 6-9-1992, div. 7, §§ 2, 4) 
Sec. 40-83. - Exemptions. 
(a)	New construction and the repair or renovation of an existing building shall be exempt from the requirements of this division when: 
(1)	The repair or renovation of the existing building does not include the replacement of the plumbing or sewage system servicing toilets, faucets or showerheads within such existing buildings; 
(2)	Such plumbing or sewage system within such existing building, because of its capacity, design, or installation, would not function properly if the toilets, faucets or showerheads required by this article were installed; 
(3)	The system is a well or gravity flow from a spring and is owned privately by an individual for use in such individual's personal residence; or 
(4)	Units to be installed are specifically designed for use by the handicapped, specifically designed to withstand unusual abuse or installation in a penal institution, or toilets for juveniles. 
(b)	The owner (or his agent) of a building undergoing new construction or repair or renovation who is entitled to an exemption under this section shall obtain the exemption by applying at the office of the building inspector for the Liberty Consolidated Planning Commission. 
(Ord. of 6-9-1992, div. 7, § 5) 
Sec. 40-84. - Enforcement; penalty. 
(a)	This division shall be enforced by the office of the building inspector of the Liberty Consolidated Planning Commission (LCPC). Citations for violations may be issued by the chief building inspector of the LCPC. 
(b)	Any person violating this division shall be tried before the county court of competent jurisdiction. Upon conviction, a violation of this division may be punished as published. 
(Ord. of 6-9-1992, div. 7, § 6) 
Secs. 40-85—40-111. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - USE REGULATIONS 

Sec. 40-112. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this division is to set out uniform requirements for users of the water system. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 2, § I) 
Sec. 40-113. - Restrictions; violations. 
(a)	The following restrictions shall apply to use of water in the city: 
(1)	No person shall use water supplied by the city water system during periods when a shortage of water exists, as determined by the city, except in accordance with conservation regulations implemented by the city. 
(2)	No person, unless authorized by the city, shall turn on or off a water supply at any meter, or at any other location or point on the city system. 
(3)	Water furnished by the city shall be used for consumption by the consumer, members of his household, and employees only. The consumer shall not sell water to any other person or permit any other person to use said water. 
(4)	Water shall not be used for irrigation, fire protection, nor other purposes except when water is available in sufficient quantity without interfering with the regular domestic consumption in the area served. 
(b)	Violations of this section shall be sufficient cause for refusal or discontinuance of service. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 2, § II, div. 4, § IV) 
Sec. 40-114. - Metering. 
(a)	All water usage from the city system will be metered by the city, except fire sprinkler systems. 
(b)	Meters shall be set on the property line and located off the public right-of-way when possible. When this is impracticable, the meter shall be located at such other places as may be approved by the mayor. 
(c)	No person shall run or extend a water line from one lot or tract of land across another lot or boundary line for the purpose of serving more than one residence or other building. 
(d)	No person, except authorized personnel, will be allowed to install, remove or handle meters. 
(e)	The first water meter shall be installed by the city at the property owner's expense. The city will keep the meter in repair which results from normal usage. During such times as the meter is inoperable, the consumer will be charged at the average daily consumption rate as established by the city based on prior bills. 
(f)	If the water meter is repaired or replaced for reasons other than failure due to normal usage, the cost of such repairs will be charged to the customer and be collectable in accordance with this article. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 2, § III) 
Sec. 40-115. - Unlawful water use. 
(a)	If water is used without the knowledge of the city, at such time as the city becomes aware of the illegal use of said water, a charge will be made against the owner of the property served for the time the water has been used, or the quantity shown by the meter to have been used, and future water service shall be immediately discontinued and will not be restored until the bill therefor is paid. 
(b)	If the customer does not pay the bill, then the landowner, if different, shall be held responsible for the charges. 
(c)	This section applies to illegal use of water from any fire hydrants. 
(d)	A penalty for such use will be assessed by the city against the illegal user. The amount of the penalty will be determined by the city. If requested by the user so charged, the city will conduct a hearing into the matter. The penalty assessed for violation of this section may include criminal sanctions under state law. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 3, § III(C)) 
Sec. 40-116. - Interruption of service in cases of emergency. 
The city may terminate or interrupt service in cases of emergency and for the repair or expansions of the water system. Advanced notice of said interruptions will be given when possible. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 1, § III(G); Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Sec. 40-117. - Disconnection of service by customer. 
When the customer desires to discontinue water service, the following procedure will apply: 
(1)	The customer shall give written notice of such fact to the city. When notified, the city shall remove the customer's meter. A new tap-in fee will be charged to a subsequent user to place the water line back into service. Customers who fail to notify the city shall be charged the minimum monthly fee. 
(2)	Upon discontinuance of water service, the city shall remove the meter and turn off the service line to the premises. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 3, § III(A), (B)) 
Secs. 40-118—40-147. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - SEWER 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 40-148. - Purpose. 
It is the purpose of this article to set forth requirements for obtaining sewer service in the city. This article also provides that the city may establish specific standards and requirements for the construction of all new or replacement sewer lines and any accessories or extensions thereto. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 1, § I) 
Sec. 40-149. - Damage prohibited. 
No person shall maliciously, willfully, or negligently break, damage, destroy, uncover, deface, or tamper with any structure, appurtenance, or equipment which is a part of the wastewater facilities. Any person violating this provision shall be subject to immediate arrest under charge of disorderly conduct. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 7.1) 
Secs. 40-150—40-166. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 40-167. - Right of entry. 
(a)	Generally. Duly authorized employees or agents bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter all properties for the purposes of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling, and testing pertinent to discharge to the public sewerage system in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 8.1) 
(b)	Private property. Duly authorized employees or agents bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter all private properties through which the city holds an easement for the purpose of, but not limited to, inspection, observation, measurement, sampling, repair, and maintenance of any portion of the wastewater facilities lying within said easement. All entry and subsequent work, if any, on said easement, shall be done in full accordance with the terms of the duly negotiated easement pertaining to the private property involved. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 8.3) 
Sec. 40-168. - Access to premises. 
Duly authorized agents shall have access at all hours to the premises of the consumer for the purpose of installing or removing city property, inspecting piping, reading and testing meters, and for any other purpose in connection with the sewer service in these facilities and enforcing the provisions of this article or any rules promulgated under the authority thereof. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 1, § III(E)) 
Sec. 40-169. - Safety standards; indemnification of private property owners. 
While performing necessary work on private property, the authorized employees or agents shall observe all safety rules applicable to the premises. The property owner or lessee shall be held harmless for injury to or death of persons and for loss or damage to its property caused by acts or omissions of the city's employees or agents against liability claims and demands for personal injury or property damage asserted against the property owner or lessee, except as such may be caused by negligence or failure of the property owner or lessee to maintain safe conditions as required by this article. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 8.2) 
Sec. 40-170. - Violations deemed misdemeanors; continuing violations. 
Violations of this article shall be a misdemeanor punishable under state law. Each day of continuing violation shall be considered a separate offense. Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall become liable to the city for any expense, loss, or damage occasioned the city by reason of violation. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 10.1) 
Sec. 40-171. - Order for corrective action; failure to obey; notice. 
(a)	In the event of violation of this article, the health officer or authorized employees may verbally instruct the owner as to the necessary corrective action. If the owner fails to carry out verbal instructions in a timely manner or if a serious violation or hazard to public health exists, the health officer or city may issue to the owner a written order stating the nature of the violation, the corrective action, and the time limit for completing the corrective action. 
(b)	The record of the mailing of said notice or order shall be prima facie evidence thereof, and failure of said owner to receive same shall in no way affect the validity of any proceedings conducted pursuant to this article. 
(c)	Failure to comply with any written order duly issued by the health officer or city pursuant to subsection (a) of this section will constitute a separate misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be punishable as provided by the laws of the state. 
(d)	Compliance with this article is required regardless of whether a written order is issued. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, §§ 10.2, 10.3) 
Sec. 40-172. - Violations and nuisances subject to suit for injunction or abatement. 
(a)	The violation of any provisions of this article, as now existing or as may be hereafter amended, may be enjoined by instituting appropriate proceedings in the name of the city for injunction in the courts of competent jurisdiction in the state. 
(b)	Any public nuisance which is injurious to the public health, safety or comfort may be abated by instituting appropriate proceedings in the name of the city for injunction in the court of competent jurisdiction in the state. 
(c)	Such actions may be maintained notwithstanding the fact that such violation also constitutes a crime, and notwithstanding that other adequate remedies at law exist. Such actions may be instituted in the name of the city. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 10.4) 
Sec. 40-173. - Demand for and scheduling of hearing. 
(a)	Upon receipt of a notice of a violation of this article or an order of the city requiring an act or thing be done or to cease, the owner of any premises then in question may, in writing, demand a hearing before the city council to present the evidence challenging the validity of the city's order. 
(b)	The owner may appear in person, by agent, or by attorney. The demand must be filed with the city clerk and made within five days from the receipt of the order being challenged. 
(c)	Upon receipt of a demand for a hearing, the city will set a date, time, and place for said hearing to be not less than 21 days from the date of filing of said demand. 
(d)	The hearing as provided for herein shall apply to any customer's complaint, dispute, or challenge of the city's rules, regulations, resolutions, ordinances, or policies. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 10.5) 
Sec. 40-174. - Rules of evidence. 
Evidence before the city of any hearing conducted pursuant to this division shall be admitted in accordance with the rules of evidence of the state superior courts; provided, however, the city may take official notice of any order, rule, regulation, or any other document, record, or entry contained in its official record or minutes for evidentiary purposes. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 10.6) 
Sec. 40-175. - City council determination final. 
For the purpose of this article, the decisions of the city council will prevail in any instance in which there is a conflict between it and the health officer on any issue of sanitation, or the lack of it, and its effect on human health or well-being. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 10.7) 
Secs. 40-176—40-203. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - CONNECTIONS AND USE 

Sec. 40-204. - Written permits required. 
No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any connections with or opening into, use, alter, or disturb any public sewer or appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the city. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 5.1) 
Sec. 40-205. - Application; fees. 
The owner or his agent shall make application for a permit on a special form furnished by the city. The permit application shall be supplemented by any plans, specifications or other information considered pertinent in the judgment of the superintendent. A permit and inspection fee as specified in the fee schedule shall be paid at the time the application is filed. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 5.2) 
Sec. 40-206. - Connection to sewer service when available; waiver of requirement. 
No person shall hereafter operate private facilities when existing or new service is available within 200 feet of the facility to be served. The city may waive this requirement for good cause shown and the city's decision in the exercise of its legislative discretion shall be controlling. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 1, § III(A)) 
Sec. 40-207. - Separate building sewers required; exception. 
A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every building, except where one building stands at the rear of another on an interior lot and no private sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building through an adjoining alley, court, yard or driveway, the front building may be extended to the rear building and the whole considered as one building sewer, but the city does not and will not assume any obligation or responsibility for damage caused by or resulting from any single connection aforementioned. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 5.4) 
Sec. 40-208. - Unauthorized connections. 
No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any connections with or opening into, use, or disturb any public sewer main or appurtenances thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the city. No connection shall be made except at a connection point approved by the city. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 1, § III(C)) 
Sec. 40-209. - Application. 
No sewer line shall be tapped except by authorized employees. An application will be made to the city prior to connection to the sewer system. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 1, § III(B)) 
Sec. 40-210. - Responsibility of property owner for costs. 
(a)	The owner of the property to be served shall be responsible for the cost, installation and maintenance of the sewer service line from the facility to be served to a point where the service line ties into the city system, which includes any portions of the service line extending on to the public right-of-way or city easement. 
(b)	The pipe from the main sewer line to the served premises shall be the property of the owner, and all repairs to such lines shall be at the owner's expense. The city shall have an easement to use any portion of the pipe located off of city property and any land adjacent thereto so long as any service is provided to the premises by the city. 
(c)	The owner shall indemnify the city from any loss or damage that may directly or indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the building sewer. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 1, § III(D); Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 2, § I(B); Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 5.3) 
Sec. 40-211. - Compliance with state health department regulations required. 
The consumer's piping and apparatus shall be installed and maintained by the consumer at the consumer's expense in a safe and efficient manner and in accordance with the sanitary regulations of the state health department. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 2, § I(A)) 
Sec. 40-212. - Right of city to revoke permission for connection. 
The city shall have the right for good cause shown to revoke or annul at any time any permit previously issued for the connection to any sewer lines, and no party shall have the right to claim damage as a result of such permit being revoked or annulled. The city reserves the right to disconnect and discontinue its service without notice for the following additional reasons: 
(1)	To prevent fraud or abuse. 
(2)	Consumer's willful disregard of the city's rules. 
(3)	Emergency repairs. 
(4)	Circumstances beyond the city's control. 
(5)	Legal proceedings. 
(6)	At the direction of public authorities. 
(7)	Strike, riot, flood, fire, or unavoidable accidents. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 1, § III(F)) 
Sec. 40-213. - Connection in floodplain prohibited. 
(a)	The city will not allow any connection to any facility located in a 100-year floodplain as designated on the relevant flood maps published by the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA), within any jurisdictional freshwater wetlands, prime farmland or endangered or threatened species habitat. 
(b)	The operating provisions for the proposed land application system by the city will restrict encroachment and disturbance into any jurisdictional wetlands found within the confines of the subject land application system as designated on the relevant maps. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 6; Ord. of 1-7-2003) 
Sec. 40-214. - Interruption of service in cases of emergency. 
The city may terminate or interrupt service in cases of emergency, and for the repair or expansions of the sewer system. Advanced notice of said interruptions will be given when possible. 
(Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 1, § III(G)) 
Sec. 40-215. - Grounds for termination of service. 
The city reserves the right to terminate water and wastewater disposal services and disconnect a customer from the system when: 
(1)	Acids or chemicals damaging to sewer lines or the treatment process are released into the public sewer causing rapid deterioration of these structures or interfering with proper conveyance and treatment of wastewater; 
(2)	A government agency informs the city that the effluent from the wastewater treatment plant is no longer of a quality permitted for discharge into a watercourse, and it is found that the customer is discharging wastewater into the public sewer that cannot be sufficiently treated or requires treatment that is not provided by the city as normal domestic treatment; or 
(3)	The customer: 
a.	Discharges industrial waste or wastewater that is in violation of the permit issued by the approving authority; 
b.	Discharges wastewater at an uncontrolled, variable rate in sufficient quantity to cause an imbalance in the wastewater treatment process; 
c.	Fails to pay monthly bills for sanitary sewer service when due; or 
d.	Repeats a discharge of prohibited wastes into public sewers. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 12.1) 
Secs. 40-216—40-238. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - FIXTURES 

Sec. 40-239. - Toilet required for disposal of human excrement. 
No person shall dispose of human excrement except in a toilet. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 3.2) 
Sec. 40-240. - Minimum toilet requirements; maintenance. 
(a)	All premises shall be provided by the owner thereof with at least one toilet. All toilets shall be kept clean and in sanitary working condition. 
(b)	The owners of all houses, buildings or properties used for human occupancy, employment, recreation or other purposes situated within the city jurisdiction and abutting on any street, alley, or right-of-way, in which there is now located or may in the future be located a public sanitary sewer, is hereby required at the owner's expense to install suitable toilet facilities herein, and to connect such facilities directly with the proper public sewer in accordance with the provisions of this article, within 30 days after the date of official notice to do so, provided that said public sewer is within 200 feet of the property line. 
(c)	Every flush toilet shall be connected to a public sewer where available or to a septic tank. Flush toilets shall be provided at all times with sufficient running water under pressure to flush the toilet clean after use. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, §§ 3.1, 3.5, 4.9) 
Sec. 40-241. - Connection of other fixtures and appliances required. 
All sinks, dishwashing machines, lavatories, basins, showerbaths, bathtubs, laundry tubs, washing machines, and similar plumbing fixtures or appliances shall be connected to the public sewer; provided that, where no sewer is available, septic tanks or other private subsurface disposal facilities approved by the health officer may be used. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 3.6) 
Secs. 40-242—40-260. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - DISCHARGE RESTRICTIONS 

Sec. 40-261. - Compliance with state and federal regulations required. 
The provisions of this article shall not be deemed as alleviating compliance with applicable state and federal regulations. Specific user charge and industrial cost recovery requirements, promulgated pursuant to federal P.L. 92-500 (which amended the federal Clean Water Act, 33 USC 1251 et seq.) shall be considered as a part of this article upon official adoption. All nonresidential users will be required to comply with pretreatment standards as outlined in 40 CFR 403. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 9.1) 
Sec. 40-262. - Conflict with rules of other jurisdictions. 
In the event a wastewater discharge is made to a publicly owned treatment works (POTW) under the jurisdiction of an approved sewer use ordinance for another governing authority, the more restrictive requirement shall prevail. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 13.3) 
Sec. 40-263. - Unlawful to discharge to natural outlets and other city areas. 
It shall be unlawful to discharge to any natural outlet within the city or in any area under the jurisdiction of the city, any wastewater or other polluted waters, including septic tank effluent or cesspool overflow to any open drain or well-penetrating, water-bearing formation, except where suitable treatment has been provided in accordance with subsequent provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 3.3) 
Sec. 40-264. - Prohibited discharges. 
The following described substances, materials, waters, or waste shall be limited in discharge to municipal systems to concentrations or quantities which will not harm either the sewers, wastewater treatment process or equipment, will not have an adverse effect on the receiving stream, or will not otherwise endanger lives, limb, public property, or constitute a nuisance. The limitations or restrictions on materials or characteristics of waste or wastewater discharged to the sanitary sewer which shall not be violated without approval of the city are as follows: 
(1)	Wastewater having a temperature higher than 150 degrees Fahrenheit (65 degrees Celsius) or wastewater which will elevate the temperature of the influent to the publicly owned treatment works (POTW) to 104 degrees Fahrenheit (40 degrees Celsius) or higher. 
(2)	Wastewater containing more than 25 milligrams per liter of petroleum oil, non-biodegradable cutting oils, or product of mineral oil origin. 
(3)	Wastewater containing more than 100 milligrams per liter of oils, fat, grease or wax, whether emulsified or not, or containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperatures between 32 degrees (0 degrees Celsius) and 150 degrees Fahrenheit (65 degrees Celsius). 
(4)	Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. Garbage grinders may be connected to sanitary sewers from homes, hotels, institutions, restaurants, hospitals, catering establishments, or similar places where garbage originates from the preparation of food in kitchens for the purpose of consumption on the premises or when served by caterers. 
(5)	All industrial discharges to the city sewer system must comply with the federal industrial pretreatment standards (40 CFR 403) and those industrial pretreatment standards developed by the state environmental protection division. 
(6)	Any waters or wastes containing taste or odor producing substances exceeding limits which may be established by the city. 
(7)	Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half-life or concentrations as may exceed limits established in compliance with applicable state or federal regulations. 
(8)	Quantities of flow, concentrations, or both which constitute a "slug." 
(9)	Waters or wastes containing substances which are not amenable to treatment or reduction by the wastewater treatment processes employed, or are amenable to treatment only to such degree that the sewage treatment plant effluent cannot meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction over discharge to the receiving waters. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 6.5) 
Sec. 40-265. - Measurements, tests, analyses and sampling. 
All measurements, tests, and analyses of the characteristics of waters and wastes to which reference is made in this article shall be determined in accordance with the latest edition of Standard Methods for the Examination of Water and Wastewater, published by the American Public Health Association. Sampling methods, location times, durations, and frequencies are to be determined on an individual basis, subject to approval by the city. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 6.11) 
Sec. 40-266. - Pretreatment of wastes. 
(a)	Required for industrial waste discharge; submittal of plans for approval. Persons discharging industrial wastes into the sewerage system may be required to pretreat such wastes. Plans for all pretreatment facilities shall be approved by the superintendent or the state environmental protection division prior to construction. At the time written plans are submitted for approval, written maintenance plans shall also be submitted and approved by the superintendent. The facilities shall be allowed to operate only as long as they are maintained in accordance with the approved maintenance plans. 
(b)	Pretreatment requirements. Pretreatment requirements shall include the following facilities as a minimum: 
(1)	Neutralization. If plans are submitted for the neutralization of strong acid or alkaline wastes, the plans shall include the necessary instrumentation and controls to ensure compliance with subsection (a) of this section at all times. 
(2)	Equalization. Holding tanks or equalization basins shall be required ahead of the receiving manhole of the city sewerage system when deemed necessary by the superintendent to prevent peak flows that exceed the capacity of the system or that result in operational problems. 
(c)	Operation and maintenance of facilities. All pretreatment facilities shall be operated and maintained continuously in satisfactory and effective operation by the owner at his expense. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 6.12) 
Sec. 40-267. - Waiver of requirements. 
There shall be no provision for the granting of variances for discharge of incompatible wastes. If a user begins to violate any of the provisions of this division, it shall be his responsibility to apply to the superintendent who can issue a temporary permit along with a compliance schedule for planning and construction of necessary treatment or pretreatment works. Each case will be carefully evaluated with respect to its effect on the wastewater treatment system and the environment prior to issuance of a temporary permit compliance schedule. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 6.13) 
Sec. 40-268. - Dilution to decrease concentration. 
Any dilution of the wastewater by the user for the purpose of decreasing the concentrations of toxic material shall be considered a violation of this division. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 6.13) 
Sec. 40-269. - Discontinuance of service for failure to comply; notice. 
Failure to comply with the provisions of this division shall be cause for the discontinuance of sewer or water service to the offending person. The procedure shall be as follows: 
(1)	A written notice, signed by the superintendent, shall be delivered personally to the person then responsible for the offending use, outlining the conditions of the wastes which violate the provision of this Code. 
(2)	In the event that the person in charge will not accept the notice, it shall be conveyed by registered mail to the responsible person. 
(3)	The person notified shall have 24 hours from the time of receipt of the notice, either personally delivered or received by registered mail, to correct the offending conditions. 
(4)	If correction is not made or a request for extension is not received by the city within 24 hours, it shall be mandatory that water and/or sewer service shall be discontinued to the offending person without further notice. 
(5)	If a request for an extension of time is received by the city within 24 hours of the notice as stated in subsection (1) of this section and if circumstances are such that in the opinion of the superintendent, the best interest of the city would be served by extending the time for correction of the offending condition, then he may grant an extension of time up to a maximum limit of 30 days. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 6.14) 
Sec. 40-270. - Responsibilities of the person discharging waste. 
(a)	It shall be the responsibility of the person discharging industrial waste into the city sewerage system to: 
(1)	Build a control structure in the discharge line from his premises, immediately prior to the entrance of the discharge line into the city sewerage system, suitable for the sampling and measuring of wastes. 
(2)	Contact the superintendent prior to operation changes which will materially alter the characteristics of the waste from the last prior sampling. 
(3)	Make timely, periodic payments to the city of surcharges for excessive loading as detailed in the city user charge system. 
(b)	Plans for a control structure must be approved by the city. The requirement for a control structure may be waived if deemed unnecessary by the city. 
(c)	In the event that no special manhole is required, the control manhole shall be considered to be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to the point at which the building sewer is connected. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 6.15) 
Secs. 40-271—40-288. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 6. - PRIVATE DISPOSAL SYSTEMS 

Sec. 40-289. - Additional requirements may be imposed by health officer. 
No statement contained in this division shall be constructed to interfere with any additional requirements that may be imposed by the health officer. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 4.14) 
Sec. 40-290. - Unlawful to construct or maintain; exceptions. 
Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be unlawful to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool, or other facility intended or used for the disposal of wastewater. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 3.4) 
Sec. 40-291. - When connection required. 
(a)	Where a public sanitary sewer is not available as provided herein, the building sewer shall be connected to a private wastewater disposal system complying with the provisions of the city and the state department of natural resources. 
(b)	Premises with private water systems shall be connected with the public sewerage system. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, §§ 4.1, 4.13) 
Sec. 40-292. - Septic tank standards. 
Septic tanks shall be constructed, repaired, altered, enlarged and maintained in accordance with plans and specifications approved by the health officer. Septic tanks shall be maintained in sanitary working order. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 4.2) 
Sec. 40-293. - Permit required; approval by health officer. 
(a)	No person shall construct, repair, alter, or enlarge any septic tank unless he shall hold a valid permit for such work issued by the health officer. The health officer may withhold the issuance of such a permit pending the inspection and approval by the health officer of the site and location of the proposed work. 
(b)	Before any septic tank or any part thereof may be covered after it has been constructed, repaired, altered, or enlarged, it shall be inspected and approved by the health officer. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 4.3) 
Sec. 40-294. - Restrictions on installation and use of subsurface disposal facilities. 
(a)	The type, capacities, location and layout of a private wastewater disposal system shall comply with all recommendations of the state department of natural resources. 
(b)	No subsurface disposal facilities shall be installed in any place where the health officer deems the use of such facilities to be a menace to human health or well-being. 
(c)	No permit shall be issued for any private wastewater disposal system employing subsurface soil absorption facilities where the area of the lot is less than 10,000 square feet. No septic tank or cesspool shall be permitted to discharge to any natural outlet. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, §§ 4.4, 4.8) 
Sec. 40-295. - Restrictions on construction and use of pit privy. 
No pit privy shall be installed in the following locations: 
(1)	Where a public sewer is accessible to the premises involved; 
(2)	In areas where the health officer deems the use of pit privies to constitute a nuisance or menace to the public health; 
(3)	Where a pit privy may pollute any water supply; or 
(4)	Where the use of pit privies is not in keeping with the standard of sanitation in adjacent areas. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 4.10) 
Sec. 40-296. - Closing and connection to public sewer. 
At such time as a public sewer becomes available to a property served by a private wastewater disposal system, a direct connection shall be made to the public sewer within 30 days after notice. Any septic tanks, cesspools, and similar private wastewater disposal facilities shall then be cleaned of sludge and filled with suitable material. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 4.6) 
Sec. 40-297. - Maintenance. 
The owners shall operate and maintain the private wastewater disposal facilities in a sanitary manner at all times and at no expense to the city. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 4.7) 
Sec. 40-298. - Discharge of septic tanks in sewer system. 
(a)	Restricted. It shall be unlawful to empty, dump, throw or otherwise discharge, into any manhole, catchbasin or other opening, into the city sewer system, or any system connected with discharging into the sewer system, the contents of any septic tank, sludge, sewage, or other similar matter or material, except as provided in subsection (b) of this section. 
(b)	Permits. The superintendent of public works or his designee is authorized to grant permits to discharge the contents of septic tanks at locations specified by the superintendent and under his supervision. Such permits may be revoked at any time if, in the opinion of the superintendent, continued dumping of such matter into the sewers will be injurious to the sewer system or treatment processes. 
(c)	Charges. A charge shall be made for the privilege of dumping the contents of septic tanks, as provided in separate rules. A record shall be kept of such dumpings and statements rendered at the first of each month, and the amount of such statements shall be payable within ten days after rendition. Failure to pay the amounts due within such ten-day period shall be cause for revoking the permit. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 4.11) 
Sec. 40-299. - Faulty system; correction. 
Any septic tank, privy, or any other sewage, industrial waste, or liquid waste disposal system located thereon that does not function in a sanitary manner shall be corrected within 30 days from the receipt of written manner and order that said system be corrected. 
(Ord. of 10-6-2009, § 4.12) 
Secs. 40-300—40-316. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - RATES, FEES AND CHARGES 

Sec. 40-317. - Debt service. 
The bond amount for the water and wastewater projects funded by the Georgia Environmental Facilities Authority (GEFA) and other revenue bonds, including all engineering and setup fees, can be shown as a separate line item on the water and wastewater bill or combined in the base charge. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-318. - Residential equivalent units. 
(a)	A residential equivalent unit is that portion of a user's facility that has an impact on the water and wastewater system equivalent to a single-family residence. The determination of a facility's residential equivalent units shall be based on estimated water consumption as shown in guidelines below or on square footage. Peak water consumption of 300 gallons per day or a floor space of 3,000 square feet shall be the equivalent of one residential unit. The method which results in the greater number of equivalent residential units shall be applied. 
(b)	The standards in the table in subsection (d) of this section shall be used in the determination of water consumption. If the table does not provide information for a particular application, the estimated water consumption shall be as calculated by the director in accordance with sound engineering practices using information available from the state EPD, USEPA, or standard reference materials commonly used for estimating flows. 
(c)	In the event a facility is made up of more than one smaller component facility, the determination of residential equivalent units shall be calculated as the sum of all components' residential equivalent units. 
(d)	In a case involving a site utilizing its own private water supply and distribution system to multiple locations resulting in the production of domestic-type wastewater only, such as employee restrooms and showers, such that reading and maintenance of meters would create excessive costs and hardship in the judgment of the director, the city may bill on flow estimates, calculated on the basis of an average flow per employee times the average number of employees at such facility, for the recovery of costs of transporting and treating the wastewater. 

 
** Add 300 gallons per machine to amount indicated if laundry or dishwashing machines are installed. 
(Amd. of 4-1-2008; Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-319. - Tap fees. 
(a)	Water and wastewater tap fees shall be charged on the basis of residential units or residential equivalent units according to the tap fees listed in the city fee schedule. Any fractional units resulting from the calculation of residential equivalent units shall be treated as a whole unit. Tap fees are in addition to the installation fees provided for in this article. 
(b)	All work done by other than city personnel shall be done only under the supervision of licensed master plumbers authorized to perform such work. The director may authorize licensed master plumbers to install connections to water or wastewater facilities upon written application. 
(c)	The director shall require that all installation is performed in accordance with specifications or standards conforming to sound engineering practices. In the event that such installation is not made in accordance with specifications or standards, the director may require the installation to be corrected or removed and reinstalled as necessary. 
(d)	Water meters shall be supplied to authorized licensed master plumbers at cost; all other related accessories for water or sewer connections may be supplied to authorized licensed master plumbers. 
(e)	The director shall require payment of installation fees as listed in the city fee schedule or reimbursement of actual costs for any installations not specifically covered. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-320. - Installation fees. 
(a)	Installation fees shall be in addition to tap fees and shall cover only connection to existing mains that are adjacent to location to be served. The actual costs of any extensions necessary shall be charged in addition to tap and installation fees. All fees and charges shall be paid by the customer or customers at whose request the connection is made. 
(b)	Water installation fees are assessed for making taps into the city water mains or water lines and installing water meters or providing water meters for plumbers to install. Fees for installation of meters up to two inches are as set forth in the city fee schedule. Installation fees for meters larger than two inches shall be charged on the basis of reimbursement to the city for all actual costs incurred in making the installation. 
(c)	Sewer installation fees are assessed for making connections to the city sewerage system and installing service lines. These fees are based on tap size and are in the amount provided in the city fee schedule. 
(d)	Installation fees for installations requiring additional facilities including, but not limited to, manholes or flow metering installations, shall be charged on the basis of reimbursement to the city for all actual costs incurred in making the installation. 
(e)	Charges for any installation not covered in standard pricing, and charges for city staff or equipment if used on private facilities, shall be as provided in the city fee schedule. All hourly charges shall include travel time to and from the job location. Work performed outside regular business hours at the request of customers shall be charged at 150 percent of the rates in the schedule. Miscellaneous charges shall include actual charges for equipment rented to perform the work.The staging charge shall be used for construction, but may be waived for other types of work at the discretion of the director. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-321. - Overhead sprinkler systems charges. 
The charge for any overhead sprinkler systems installed in any facilities inside or outside the city limits other than single family residences shall be based on the square footage of the facility in the amount set forth in the city fee schedule. . 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-322. - Deposits. 
(a)	Deposits shall be 2½ times the monthly bill for all services, as estimated by the director using whatever data may be available, subject to the minimum deposit amounts provided in the city fee schedule. . 
(b)	Deposits may be waived or reduced if evidence is produced that the customer has a good record of payment or that the customer would reasonably be expected to pay all bills promptly. 
(c)	In the event a deposit is waived or is less than 2½ times the monthly bill for all services for whatever reason, and that the customer is delinquent in payment of one or more bills, the deposit for that customer's account or accounts may be required to be increased to 2½ times the monthly bill for all services. Such increased deposits may be required to be paid in full before reconnection of service. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-323. - Account establishment or transfer fee. 
In addition to the fees and deposits otherwise provided hereinabove, each applicant for service shall pay in advance an account establishment charge in the amount provided in the city fee schedule for either new service or transfer of service from one location to another. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-324. - Administration charge. 
An administration charge in the amount provided in the city fee schedule will be charged to each account for meter reading, the preparation of the water and wastewater bill and other administrative duties. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-325. - Monthly use charges. 
The rates for monthly water and wastewater use shall be as provided in the city fee schedule. 
Sec. 40-326. - Adjustments in billing. 
The director is authorized to make equitable adjustments in billings for wastewater services only in cases where leaks in pipes and plumbing facilities result in increased billings without fault on the part of the customer. Such adjustments shall be made based on an average of prior billings only after repairs have been made as certified by a licensed plumber, and shall be limited to three months' billings. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-327. - Late fee. 
In the event a utility bill has not been paid by the past due date printed on the bill, the account may be subject to an additional late fee in the amount provided in the city fee schedule. Late fees may be incurred whether or not the service is disconnected. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-328. - Disconnection, reconnection and related charges. 
(a)	In the event that service has been cut off for nonpayment of any city utility bill or other action resulting in unauthorized use of city services, service shall not be restored until the unpaid bill and service fees provided by this section are satisfied. 
(b)	Before service is restored, the service fees provided in the city fee schedule shall be paid by the user cumulatively for each action taken to prevent unauthorized use of city services. 
(c)	Payment of fees for reconnection or other fees for delinquency in payment or unauthorized use or tampering shall not exempt any user from any civil or criminal action resulting from violations of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Sec. 40-329. - Charges for unauthorized meter tampering. 
If any action taken by unauthorized persons inside a meter box causes damages to a curb stop or a cover or lock connected to a curb stop, the resident or customer responsible for the premises shall be charged a fee in the amount provided in the city fee schedule for each incident in addition to other fees and charges. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2008) 
Secs. 40-330—40-346. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - SPECIAL ASSESSMENTS 

Sec. 40-347. - Authorized. 
Whenever a water or sewer line is constructed in an established residential area of the city in which such service was not previously available to residents of said area, or in the case of a public health hazard or extreme hardship, the city council may, in exercise of its discretion, by resolution employ the procedure provided in this article for the collection of impact or tap-in fees in order to extend service to an existing house or building in said area. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I) 
Sec. 40-348. - Authority to levy assessment. 
Upon application of the owner of the property lying in the unserved area, or in case of a public health hazard or extreme hardship in any area, the city council may approve the connection of the property to a water or sewer line to the property without the payment in full of all tap-in or impact fees. Instead, the city council shall levy an assessment against the property to be served and the owner thereof for the amount of the impact and tap-in fee which shall constitute a lien upon the property from the date of adoption of the resolution. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I) 
Sec. 40-349. - Clerk to maintain docket. 
The city clerk shall keep a docket of convenient form and size, with property index, in which there shall be registered all such assessments against property for water or sewer, which docket shall be posted immediately upon the passage by the city council of a resolution authorizing the connection of any water or sewer line. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I;) 
Sec. 40-350. - Installment payments; failure to execute agreement or pay. 
(a)	The owner of the property shall be required to pay in cash or by certified check, within 60 days, not less than 25 percent of the amount of such assessment. The remainder, after deduction of such payment, may upon request of the property owner, be divided into not more than three equal annual installments maturing one, two and three years respectively from the date of the initial payment and the execution of an installment agreement; provided, that proper documentation evidencing the extension of time of repayment shall be executed by the owner of the property in a form acceptable to the city. 
(b)	Should the owner of any property against which an assessment has been levied fail either to execute the instrument required or to pay the same in cash within 60 days, an execution shall issue forthwith against the property to which the service has been provided and the owner thereof. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I) 
Sec. 40-351. - Recordation of installment agreement. 
The installment agreement shall be recorded in the office of the clerk of the superior court of the county and shall contain an acknowledgment of the owner that said assessment constitutes a valid and legally enforceable lien against his property. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I) 
Sec. 40-352. - Effect of extension of time for payment. 
No extension of time for the payment of any assessment shall affect the validity of the assessment or the right of the city, or its assigns, to proceed to enforce the same against the property and the owner thereof. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I) 
Sec. 40-353. - Interest. 
The unpaid portion of the assessment shall bear interest from date of the assessment until paid at the rate of 12 percent per annum on the unpaid balance. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I) 
Sec. 40-354. - Default. 
In case of default in any installment, the entire assessment including accrued interest shall become due and payable forthwith. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I) 
Sec. 40-355. - Recordation of executions. 
All executions issued against property and the owner thereof for such assessments shall immediately be recorded on the general execution docket in the aforesaid clerk's office. The execution shall be collected by the city following the same procedure as for other amounts due the city for assessments. . 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I) 
Sec. 40-356. - City's right to transfer and assign indebtedness. 
The evidence of the indebtedness shall be negotiable in form, and the city, free and clear of any and all encumbrances of title or claims of title by the owner, shall have the right to transfer and assign the same to third parties. 
(Ord. of 9-6-1988, div. 6, § I; Ord. of 7-6-1999, div. 5, § I)

(RESERVED)
